Prohibition of Facing Qibla during Istinja: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on prohibition with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the qibla during istinja inside a building and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The general prohibition of facing qibla in istinja applies even inside buildings according to the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does the prohibition of facing or turning one's back to the qibla during relieving oneself apply inside a building? The Hanafi school holds it is makruh tahrimi in all circumstances, while Imam al-Shafi'i exempts buildings. We will trace the evidence from the hadith and the usul principles behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling for defecation and urination separately, and note that it applies even inside buildings.
For defecation, both facing and turning back are makruh tahrimi; for urination, only facing is makruh tahrimi.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State Imam al-Shafi'i's view that the prohibition is limited to open spaces and does not apply inside buildings.
The opposing dalil is the phrase 'except when built up' in the hadith of Abu Ayyub.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Cite the hadith of Salman (no exception) and the general command in the hadith of Abu Ayyub, interpreting the exception as a dispensation.
The Hanafi school prioritizes the unrestrictive hadith and classifies the prohibition as makruh tahrimi due to zanni thubut.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i exception
Explain how the Hanafi school handles the apparent exception: it is understood as referring to cases where facing qibla is unavoidable, not as a general license.
The hadith of Salman is more explicit and does not include the exception, so it is considered stronger.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, a Hanafi will avoid facing qibla even in a bathroom, while a Shafi'i will not consider it objectionable inside a toilet.
This affects daily practice, especially in modern bathrooms oriented towards Makkah.

And he should not speak except for necessity. (58) It is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) to face the qibla or turn one's back to it. Evidence: ... Translation of (58): And facing the qibla and turning one's back to it is prohibitively disliked, even if in a building. Explanation: For defecation, both facing and turning back are prohibitively disliked; for urination, facing is prohibitively disliked but turning one's back is not disliked. According to Hanafis, it is disliked even in a building, while Imam Shafi'i does not consider it disliked in a building, only in open space. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari: When any of you goes to relieve himself, do not face the qibla nor turn his back to it. (2) Hadith of Salman: He forbade us from facing the qibla for defecation or urination. And this hadith does not include the exception for buildings, so it is disliked even in a building. Vocabulary: Istiqbal: facing the qibla; istidbar: turning one's back; bunyan: building. And even in a building.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the ruling of facing or turning one's back to the qibla during istinja (relieving oneself). The text begins with a general ruling that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to do so, and then clarifies that according to the Hanafi school this applies even when one is inside a building. The Shafi'i school holds that inside a building it is not disliked, only in open spaces. The Hanafi position is supported by the general hadith of Salman which does not exempt buildings, and the exception in the hadith of Abu Ayyub ("except when built up") is interpreted as a dispensation (rukhsah) but the stronger evidence is the general prohibition. The text also includes a hadith prohibiting speaking during istinja, as part of the broader etiquette.

Key Terms
استقبال القبلة (istiqbal al-qibla): Facing the direction of the Kaaba during the act of relieving oneself.
استدبار القبلة (istidbar al-qibla): Turning one's back to the qibla during the act.
مكروه تحريمي (makruh tahrimi): An act which is prohibited by a zanni (probable) proof; it is sinful to perform but not as severe as haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of facing the qibla while defecating inside a building?
A) Makruh tahrimi
B) Mubah
C) Sunnah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits facing or turning one's back to the qibla during istinja even inside buildings, based on general hadith evidence.

Prohibition of Facing Sun, Moon, and Wind Direction during Istinja
Ruling on prohibition of facing sun, moon, and wind direction during istinja with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on facing the sun, moon, and wind direction during istinja, identify the proof from hadith, and explain the rationale behind the dislike.

Core Idea
Facing the sun, moon, or wind direction while urinating is makruh tanzih — a respect for Allah's creation and a safeguard against physical impurity.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding additional adab of istinja. The text establishes that facing the sun, moon, or the wind direction is disliked (makruh) during urination and defecation. We will explore the textual evidence and the reasoning behind this ruling, which balances reverence for Allah's honored creation with practical hygiene.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific act is being ruled upon? The act is facing the sun, moon, or wind direction while performing istinja (urination/defecation). The ruling is makruh (disliked).
The text uses the term 'makruh' without qualification; Hanafi scholars classify it as makruh tanzih.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? Two hadith: (1) Abu Hurairah: 'The Prophet disliked urinating into the wind.' (2) Abu Musa: The Prophet chose a spot at the base of a wall to urinate, then instructed to choose a suitable place.
The hadith are from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The first hadith uses 'يكره' (disliked), which in Hanafi usul indicates karahah (dislike). The second hadith implies avoiding spray by choosing a proper place.
The Prophet's action of dislike is a valid basis for makruh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement among schools? The Shafi'i school generally does not have a specific prohibition for facing sun/moon/wind unless it leads to impurity.
The difference is one of emphasis; both schools respect the principles.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
What is the relied-upon position? The mufta bihi is makruh tanzih, based on the evidence and the rationale of respect and hygiene.
No intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded for this ruling.

Source Text

ترجمه : (۵۹) اور سورج اور چاند کا استقبال اور ہوا کے رخ پر بھی مکروہ ہے۔
[PAGE_84 continuation] ولو في البنيان (۵۹) واستقبال عين شمس والقمر ومهب الريح .
تشریح : سورج اور چاند اللہ کی محترم مخلوق ہے اس لئے اس کی طرف پیشاب کر کے اس کی توہین نہ کرے۔ اور ہوا کے رخ پر اس لئے پیشاب نہ کرے کہ اس سے چھینٹا اپنے جسم پر آئے گا۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرۃ قال كان رسول الله الا الله يكره البول في الهواء (سنن بیہقی، باب النهي عن التخلي في طريق الناس فلهم ، ج اول ص ۱۵۹ نمبر ۴۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہوا کے رخ پر پیشاب نہ کرے کیونکہ اس کا چھینٹا خود پیشاب کرنے والے پر پڑے گا۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ فکتب اليه ابو موسی انی كنت مع رسول الله الله الله ذات يوم فأراد ان يبول فأتى دمثا في اصل جدار فبال ثم قال له اذا اراد أحدكم أن يبول فليرتد لبوله موضعا - ابوداود شریف، باب الرجل یبو البولہ، ص۱۳، نمبر ۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پیشاب کے لئے کسی مناسب جگہ کا انتخاب کرے جس میں چھینٹا جسم پر نہ پڑے۔
Translation: (59) And facing the sun, the moon, and the direction of the wind is also disliked (makruh). [Page 84] And even if in a building? (59) And facing the sun, moon, and direction of the wind. Explanation: The sun and moon are honored creations of Allah, so one should not dishonor them by urinating towards them. And one should not urinate facing the wind because the spray will come back onto his body. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Abu Hurairah: The Prophet disliked urinating into the wind. (2) Hadith of Abu Musa: The Prophet chose a spot at the base of a wall to urinate, then said: When one of you wants to urinate, let him choose a place for his urine.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This lesson presents a ruling with proof regarding additional etiquettes of istinja: it is makruh (disliked) to face the sun, moon, or the direction of the wind while relieving oneself. The explanation provides the rationale: the sun and moon are noble creations, and facing the wind can cause urine to splash back. The hadith evidence includes a narration from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet disliked urinating into the wind, and another from Abu Musa indicating the importance of choosing a suitable spot to avoid spray. The text clearly marks this as a ruling of karahah (dislike), not prohibition.

Key Terms
مهب الريح (mahabb al-rih): The direction from which the wind blows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it shows disrespect to the wind
B) Because the urine spray may come back onto the person
C) Because the wind may carry impurity to others
D) There is no specific reason given

Key Takeaway
Facing the sun, moon, or wind direction while attending to nature is makruh tanzih in the Hanafi school, based on prophetic example and practical wisdom.

Prohibited Places for Urinating/Defecating: Water, Shade, Holes, Pathways, and Under Fruit Trees
Ruling on prohibition of urinating/defecating in various harmful locations with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five prohibited locations for relieving oneself and identify the harm-based rationale, citing the relevant hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Urinating/defecating in public spaces like water, shade, holes, pathways, and under fruit trees is makruh tahrimi due to harm to people and disrespect.

This lesson examines five specific locations where relieving oneself is prohibited in the Hanafi school. The ruling is based on explicit hadith evidence, emphasizing social responsibility and respect for the environment and others. Understanding these prohibitions helps a Muslim avoid causing harm and incurring sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is urinating or defecating in any of the five specified places: stagnant water, shaded resting areas, holes in the ground, public pathways, and under fruit-bearing trees. The Hanafi ruling is that this is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; it is sinful but not established with absolute certainty.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites three hadith: (1) Prohibition of urinating in stagnant water (Tirmidhi), (2) Hadith of 'the two curses'—avoid relieving oneself in pathways or shade (Muslim), (3) Prohibition of urinating in a hole because it may be a dwelling of jinn (Abu Dawud).
The prohibition under fruit trees is included in the list but not explicitly proven by these hadith; it is derived from similar harm-based reasoning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibitions (لا يبولن, اتقوا, نهى) indicate a strong prohibition. In Hanafi usul, a command to avoid (nahy) generally indicates tahrim (prohibition) unless there is evidence to lower it. Here, the harm to people supports the stronger classification.
Other schools may interpret the same hadith as indicating a lesser degree (makruh tanzih).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school may consider these acts as makruh tanzih (slightly disliked) rather than makruh tahrimi. This is a valid difference in usul principles regarding the interpretation of prohibitive language.
The practical difference is in the severity of sin; the act is still discouraged.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi mufta bihi is makruh tahrimi, based on the strength of the hadith and the overarching principle of avoiding harm (darar). This position is well-established in Zahir al-Riwayah.
The ruling applies to both men and women.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۲۰) اور مکروہ ہے کہ پیشاب اور پیخانہ پانی میں، سایہ میں سوراخ میں ، اور راستے پر اور پھل دار درخت کے نیچے کرے۔
تشریح : ان مقامات پر پیخانہ اور پیشاب کرنا اس لئے مکروہ ہے کہ اس سے انسانوں کو نقصان ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) پانی میں پیشاب کرنے کی ممانعت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی هـريــة عـن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لا يبولن أحدكم فى الماء الدائم ثم يتوضأ منه - ( ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی کراهية البول فی الماء الراكد ص ۱۹، نمبر ۶۸ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانی میں پیشاب نہ کرے، کیونکہ اس سے پھر استعمال کرنے میں کراہیت ہوگی۔(۲) سایہ میں پیشاب اور پیخانہ کرنے کی ممانعت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابى هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : اتقوا اللعانين قالوا و ما الـلـعـانـان يـا رســول الله ! قال الذي يتخلى في طريق الناس او في ظلهم ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب النھی عن انتخلى في الطريق و الظلال ص ۱۲۷، نمبر ۶۱۸/۲۶۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ راستے میں اور سائے میں پیشاب نہ کرے۔ (۳) سوراخ میں پیشاب کرنے کی ممانعت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن سرجس ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى ان يبال في الجحر ، قال : قالوا لقتادة ما يكره من البول في الجحر ؟ قال كان يقول انها مساكن الجن ۔(ابوداود شریف، باب النھی عن البول في البحر ص ۱۶ نمبر ۲۹) جمہب الریح: ہوا چلنے کا رخ۔ یتغوط فائط سے مشتق ہے، پیچلی زمین، یہاں ترجمہ ہے پیخانہ کرے۔ الظل : سایہ۔
Translation: (60) And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, in the shade, in a hole, on a pathway, and under a fruit-bearing tree. Explanation: Doing so in these places is disliked because it harms people. Evidence: (1) Prohibition of urinating in water: The Prophet said: Let none of you urinate in stagnant water then perform wudu from it. (2) Prohibition of urinating/defecating in shade: The Prophet said: Avoid the two curses: relieving oneself in people's pathways or in their shade. (3) Prohibition of urinating in a hole: The Prophet forbade urinating in a hole, as it is said to be dwellings of jinn. Vocabulary: direction of wind; yataghawwat: to defecate; al-zill: shade.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This lesson presents a ruling with proof regarding places where it is makruh to relieve oneself. The text lists five specific locations: water (especially stagnant water), shaded areas where people sit, holes in the ground (which may be dwellings of jinn), public pathways, and beneath fruit-bearing trees. The commentary explains that the common reason is causing harm or inconvenience to humans (or disrespect to jinn). The hadith evidence includes: (1) prohibition of urinating in still water due to future use, (2) the hadith of 'the two curses' referring to pathways and shade, and (3) prohibition of urinating in holes because they are habitats of jinn. The lesson emphasizes social responsibility and respect for the environment.

Key Terms
اللعانین (al-lu'anan): Two things that bring about curses: relieving oneself in pathways and in shaded resting places.
الجحر (al-juhur): A hole or burrow in the ground, often inhabited by animals or jinn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of 'the two curses' (al-lu'anan), what two places are specifically mentioned?
A) Water and shade
B) Pathways and shade
C) Holes and pathways
D) Fruit trees and water

Key Takeaway
Relieving oneself in public water sources, pathways, shade, holes, and under fruit trees is prohibited as makruh tahrimi due to potential harm to people and social responsibility.

The First Fard of Wudu: Washing the Face
Ruling with proof on the first fard of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four fard acts of wudu, define the boundaries of the face, and identify the Qur'anic and hadith proofs for washing the face.

Core Idea
Washing the face is the first fard of wudu; its boundaries and obligation are proven by the Quran and Sunnah.

This lesson focuses on the ruling that washing the face is the first of four fard (obligatory) acts of wudu. The author defines its precise boundaries and provides two strong proofs: a clear Qur'anic command and a Prophetic demonstration. Understanding this is foundational for valid wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that washing the face is classified as a fard (obligatory) act of wudu. In Hanafi fiqh, fard means omission invalidates wudu.
The author states it is the first of four pillars (arkan).
2
Define the boundaries of the face
The length from the top of the forehead (where hair grows) to the bottom of the chin, and the width between the two ear lobes. This includes the entire front of the face.
This ensures the entire face is washed; partial washing is insufficient.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
The verse Al-Ma'idah 5:6 commands: 'wash your faces' (faghsilu wujuhakum). The imperative form indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The verse is the primary evidence for the obligation.
4
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith of Uthman ibn Affan (narrated by Humran) shows the Prophet's method of wudu, which includes washing the face three times and confirms it as an integral part.
The hadith also demonstrates the practice is sunnah thrice, but the obligation is once.
5
Understand the Hanafi usul principle
A direct command (amr) from the Quran or mutawatir Sunnah indicates fard unless there is evidence to lower it. Here, no such evidence exists, so washing the face is fard.
This is why the school considers it a fard, not just wajib or sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اركان الوضوء اربعة وهى فرائضه. الاول غسل الوجة وحده طولا من مبدأ سطح الجبهة الى اسفل الذقن وحده عرضا ما بين شحمتى الاذنين. قال الله تعالى: {يا أيها الذين آمنوا إذا قمتم إلى الصلاة فاغسلوا وجوهكم وأيديكم إلى المرافق وامسحوا برءوسكم وأرجلكم إلى الكعبين} [المائدة:6]. وعن حمران مولى عثمان أنه رأى عثمان بن عفان دعا بإناء، فأفرغ على كفيه ثلاث مرار فغسلهما، ثم ادخل يمينه في الاناء فمضمض واستنثر، ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا ويديه إلى المرفقين ثلاث مرار، ثم مسح برأسه، ثم غسل رجليه ثلاث مرار إلى الكعبين، ثم قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من توضأ نحو وضوئى هذا ثم صلى ركعتين لا يحدث فيهما نفسه غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه.
The pillars of wudu are four and they are its obligations. The first is washing the face: its length from the beginning of the surface of the forehead to the bottom of the chin, and its width between the two ear lobes. Allah Most High said: {O you who believe! When you rise for prayer, wash your faces and your hands to the elbows, and wipe your heads, and (wash) your feet to the ankles} [al-Ma'idah 5:6]. And from Humran, the freed slave of ‘Uthman, that he saw ‘Uthman ibn ‘Affan call for a vessel, pour water over his hands three times and wash them, then put his right hand into the vessel, rinse his mouth and nose, then wash his face three times and his hands to the elbows three times, then wipe his head, then wash his feet three times to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak‘ats without letting his mind wander, his previous sins will be forgiven.'
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof statement on the four fard (obligatory) acts of wudu in the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that the arkan (pillars) of wudu are four and they are its fara’id (obligations). In Hanafi fiqh, the terms rukn (pillar) and fard (obligation) are used interchangeably here, meaning that these acts are integral to the validity of wudu; omitting any of them invalidates it. The first fard is washing the face, and the author specifies its boundaries: lengthwise from the top of the forehead (where hair growth begins) to the bottom of the chin, and widthwise between the two ear lobes. This definition ensures that the entire face is covered. Then the author provides two proofs. The primary proof is the Qur’anic verse from Surah al-Ma’idah (5:6), which explicitly commands washing the face, hands to the elbows, wiping the head, and washing the feet to the ankles. The second proof is a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari narrated by Humran, in which ‘Uthman ibn ‘Affan demonstrates the Prophet’s ﷺ method of wudu, including washing the face three times. This hadith also indicates that washing the face is an established practice from the Prophet ﷺ. In the Hanafi school, the boundaries of the face are considered as stated: from the hairline to the chin, and between the ears. This is derived from the same hadith evidence and the practice of the Companions.

Key Terms
ركن الوضوء (rukn al-wudu): An integral act of wudu; omission invalidates wudu. In this text, it is synonymous with fard.
غسل الوجه (ghasl al-wajh): Washing the face with water flowing over the skin, from the forehead to the chin and between the ears.
فرض (fard): An obligation established by a definitive proof (dalil qat'i); omission invalidates the act and incurs sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first fard act of wudu?
A) Washing the hands to the elbows
B) Wiping the head
C) Washing the face
D) Washing the feet to the ankles

Key Takeaway
Washing the face is the first fard of wudu; its boundaries are from the hairline to the chin and between the ears, established by Quran and Sunnah.

The Four Obligatory Acts of Wudu
Lists the four fard acts of wudu with Quranic and Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four fard acts of wudu and explain their Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Wudu has four fard acts: face, hands, head wipe, feet; omission invalidates wudu.

This lesson establishes the mandatory elements of wudu according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these four acts is fundamental because without any one of them, wudu is invalid. The lesson presents the Quranic verse and a prophetic practice as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four acts
Read the list: washing the face, washing the hands including elbows, wiping a quarter of the head, and washing the feet including ankles. Memorize them.
These are the only fard acts; all other actions are sunnah.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find verse 5:6 in the passage. Note the imperative verbs (فاغسلوا, امسحوا) which indicate obligation according to Hanafi usul.
The verse explicitly commands these four actions.
3
Understand the Hanafi definition of fard
The passage defines fard as something without which the act cannot be done. If any fard is omitted, wudu is invalid.
This is a key conceptual distinction.
4
Observe the hadith evidence
The hadith of Uthman shows the Prophet's practice confirms these four limbs. This reinforces the Quranic command.
The hadith also shows the order and repetition, but that is not fard.
5
Distinguish fard from sunnah
The passage explicitly states that the rest of wudu actions are sunnah. For example, rinsing the mouth is sunnah, not fard.
This prevents confusion about what is required.

Section on Wudu. (63) The pillars of wudu are four, and they are its obligatory acts. (24) First: washing the face, its length from the beginning of the surface of the forehead to the lower part of the chin, its width between the two earlobes. Translation: (63) The pillars of wudu are four, which are also called fard. Explanation: That without which something cannot be done is called fard. In wudu, these four things are fard: [1] washing the face, [2] washing the hands including the elbows, [3] wiping a quarter of the head, and [4] washing the feet including the ankles; the rest are sunnah. Proof: There are four fard in wudu; their evidence is this verse: 'O you who believe, when you rise to prayer, wash your faces and your hands to the elbows, and wipe your heads, and [wash] your feet to the ankles. And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves.' Surah Al-Ma'idah (5) verse 6. This verse mentions four limbs. (2) This hadith also mentions these four limbs: Humran, the freed slave of Uthman, informed him that he saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel, then poured water on his hands three times and washed them, then put his right hand into the vessel, rinsed his mouth and nose, then washed his face three times and his hands to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without talking to himself, will have his previous sins forgiven.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter on Wudu three times, p. 32, no. 159; Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on the description of the Prophet's wudu, p. 26, no. 108)

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, stating the obligatory acts (fard) of wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author lists four acts: washing the face, washing the hands including elbows, wiping the head (a quarter), and washing the feet including ankles. The term 'fard' is defined as something without which the act is invalid. The primary proof is from Quran 5:6, which explicitly commands these four actions. Additionally, a hadith of Uthman (narrated by Humran) shows the Prophet's practice. Note that the Hanafi school considers wiping the head as an obligation (fard) but with the minimum of a quarter of the head; other schools differ on the extent. The footnote clarifies that all other actions of wudu are sunnah, not fard.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): An obligatory act required for the validity of wudu; omission invalidates the wudu.
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of wudu; synonymous with fard in this context.

Key Takeaway
The four fard acts of wudu are washing the face, hands to elbows, wiping a quarter of the head, and washing the feet to ankles; these are obligatory upon every Muslim before prayer.

Washing the Face: Definition and Limits
Defines the boundaries of the face in wudu and provides supporting Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise boundaries of the face in wudu and explain the hadith evidence that establishes these limits.

Core Idea
The face in wudu is from hairline to below the chin and from earlobe to earlobe.

The first fard act of wudu is washing the face. But where exactly does the face begin and end? This lesson defines the boundaries precisely, supported by three authentic hadiths that show the Prophet's practice. Understanding these limits ensures your wudu is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that washing the face is fard (obligatory) in wudu. The text states it is the first fard.
Ruling: fard 'ayn – omission invalidates wudu.
2
Determine the length limit
From the arabic/urdu text: the length is from the beginning of the forehead (where hair growth ends) to below the chin. The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows water poured from forehead and flowing down to chin.
Upper limit: hairline (not the top of the head). Lower limit: below the chin (not the neck).
3
Determine the width limit
The width extends from one earlobe to the other. The text mentions 'shahmat al-udhun' (earlobe). The hadith of Ibn Umar mentions rubbing the cheeks, indicating they are included within the width.
Width includes the cheeks but not the ears themselves.
4
Understand the inclusion of the beard
The hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir and Ibn Umar show that the Prophet combed his beard and rubbed under it. This proves that the beard is part of the face; water must reach the skin beneath it. Combing suffices if water reaches roots.
The beard does not extend the boundaries; it lies within the defined area.
5
Synthesize the complete definition
Combine length and width: the face is a rectangle from hairline to below the chin, and between the two earlobes. Every part of this area must be washed. The neck, ears, and inside mouth are excluded.
This is the Hanafi position, agreed upon by all major schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۶۴) پہلا چہرے کا دھونا ہے اور لمبائی میں اس کی حد پیشانی کے شروع سے تھوڑی کے نیچے تک، اور چوڑائی میں دونوں کانوں کی لوتک۔ تشریح : سر کا بال جہاں سے اگنا ختم ہوتا ہے وہاں سے شروع ہو کر تھوڑی کے نیچے تک چہرے کی لمبائی کی حد ہے، اور ایک کان کی لو سے دوسرے کان کی لو تک چوڑائی میں اس کی حد ہے۔ وجه : (ا) عن ابن عباس قال دخل على على یعنی ابی طالب و قد اهرق الماء ..... ثم أخذ بكفه اليمنى قبضة من ماء فصبها على ناصيته فتركها تستن على وجهه ابوداود شریف، باب صفة وضوء النبی ، ص ۲۷، نمبر ۱۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پیشانی کے شروع سے ، تھوڑی کے نیچے تک پانی بہایا ، جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ یہ وضو کی حد ہے (۲) عن عمار بن ياسر قال رأيت رسول الله الا الله يخلل لحيته - ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی تخلیل اللحية ص ۱۳، نمبر ۴۲۹ ابوداود شریف، باب تخلیل اللحیة، ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۱۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ڈاڑھی میں خلال کرتے تھے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ڈاڑھی کے نیچے تک وضو کی حد ہے۔ (۳) عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا توضأعرک عارضیه ثم شبك لحيته بأصابعه من تحتها - (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء تخلیل اللحیة، ص ۶۳ نمبر ۴۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دونوں گالوں کو رگڑتے تھے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں گال وضو میں داخل ہیں۔ لغت : مبداً: شروع۔ جبہتہ : پیشانی۔ الذقن تھوڑی ۔ شحمہ کان کی لو، چر بی۔اذ نین: اذن کی تنثنیہ ہے، کان۔
Translation: (64) First is washing the face, and its length is from the beginning of the forehead to below the chin, and its width is between the two earlobes. Explanation: The length of the face is from where the hair of the head stops growing to below the chin; its width is from one earlobe to the other. Proofs: (1) From Ibn Abbas that he entered upon Ali (meaning Abu Talib) while he had poured water... then he took a handful of water with his right hand and poured it over his forehead and let it run down his face (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on the description of the Prophet's wudu, p. 27, no. 117). This hadith indicates that water was poured from the forehead to below the chin, so that is the limit. (2) From Ammar ibn Yasir: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) combing his beard (Sunan Ibn Majah, Chapter on combing the beard, p. 13, no. 429; Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter on combing the beard, p. 131, no. 145) - this shows that the beard is included in the face and must be washed. (3) From Ibn Umar: When the Prophet performed wudu, he would rub his cheeks then interlace his fingers under his beard (Sunan Ibn Majah, Chapter on combing the beard, p. 63, no. 432). This shows that both cheeks are included in the face. Vocabulary: Mabda': beginning; Jabhat: forehead; Adhqan: chin; Shahma: earlobe; Udhun: ear.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed definition of the first fard act: washing the face. It specifies the length from the top of the forehead (where hair growth begins) to the bottom of the chin, and the width between the two earlobes. This includes the entire surface area of the face, including the cheeks, chin, and forehead. The neck is not included. The rulings are supported by three hadiths: Ibn Abbas's narration shows water flowing from forehead to chin; Ammar's narration indicates the beard must be combed (implying water must reach the skin underneath); Ibn Umar's narration shows rubbing the cheeks. These proofs establish the precise boundaries and confirm that the beard and cheeks are part of the face for wudu.

Key Terms
وجه (wajh): The face, defined by specific boundaries: from the hairline to the chin in length, and between the two earlobes in width.
شحمة أذن (shahmat al-udhun): Earlobe, the fleshy part of the ear that hangs down. The width of the face extends to the earlobes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The eyebrows
B) The hairline (where forehead begins)
C) The nose bridge
D) The top of the head

Key Takeaway
The face in wudu is precisely defined: length from hairline to below chin, width between earlobes; every part within must be washed, and the beard requires combing to reach the skin.

The Second, Third, and Fourth Fard Acts of Wudu
States three fard acts of wudu with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three fard acts of wudu (hands to elbows, feet to ankles, wiping part of head) and cite the Hanafi proofs for including the elbows and ankles.

Core Idea
The elbows and ankle bones are fard to wash in wudu — the Prophet explicitly included them.

This passage completes the list of fard acts in wudu from the previous lesson. It addresses the second, third, and fourth fards: washing hands with elbows, washing feet with ankles, and wiping part of the head. The author provides hadith evidence to confirm the inclusion of the joints.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
List the three fard acts mentioned in the passage.
They are numbered (65), (66), (67) in the text.
2
Understand the inclusion
Note that the elbows and ankles are explicitly included in the washing. The term 'with' (مع) indicates they must be washed.
The ankle bones (ka'bayn) refer to the protruding bones on each side of the foot.
3
Examine the proof for elbows
Review the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah and the athar of 'Ata. Both show that the Prophet poured water over his elbows, confirming the elbows are part of the wash.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Daraqutni and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
4
Examine the proof for ankles
Review the hadith of Humran (via Uthman) and the hadith of Abu Hurairah. Both show washing up to the ankles or shins, establishing the ankles are included.
The hadith of Humran is also cited earlier in the wudu discussion.
5
Note the head wiping
Recognize that the fard for the head is wiping part of it. The text says 'wiping some of the head' and the Hanafi school specifies a quarter as the minimum.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider three fingers as sunnah, but the relied-upon view is a quarter as fard.

ترجمه : (۶۵) دوسرا فرض دونوں ہاتھوں کو کہنیوں سمیت دھونا ہے۔
تشریح : دونوں ہاتھوں کے دھونے میں کہنیاں داخل ہیں، اس کی دلیل اوپر آیت اور حدیث گزرگئی۔
وجه : (ا) عن جابر بن عبد الله قال كان رسول الله الله الله اذا توضأ ادار الماء على مرفقیه (دارقطنی ، باب وضوء رسول الله ، ج اول ص ۸۶ نمبر ۲۶۸ رسن للبقی ، باب ادخال المرفقين في الوضوء ، ج اول ،ص ۹۳، نمبر ۶ ۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کہنیاں دھونے میں داخل ہیں۔ (۲) قلت لعطاء : فاغسلوا وجوهكم وايديكم الى المرافق . فيما يغسل ؟ قال : نعم ، لا شک فی ذالک۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، جلد اول، باب غسل الذراعین ص ۵، نمبر ۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ بلا شبہ مرفقین دھونے میں داخل ہیں
ترجمه : (۶۶) تیسرا فرض دونوں پاؤں کو ٹخنوں سمیت دھونا ہے۔
تشریح : دونوں پاؤں کو ٹخنوں سمیت دھونا فرض ہے، اور ٹخنہ دھونے میں شامل ہے، اور اس ٹخنے سے اوپر والا ٹخنہ مراد ہے نیچے والا ٹخنہ مراد نہیں ہے۔ اس کے لئے بھی آیت اور حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔
وجه : (۱) ان حمران مولى عثمان اخبره انه رأى عثمان بن عفان دعا باناء ، فافرغ على كفيه ثلاث مرار فغسلهما ، ثم ادخل يمينه فى الاناء فمضمض واستنثر ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا و يديه الى المرفقين ثلاث مرار صلى الله ،ثم مسح برأسه ،ثم غسل رجليه ثلاث مرار الى الكعبين ، ثم قال : قال رسول الله علم : من توضأ نحو وضوئى هذا ثم صلى ركعتين لا يحدث فيهما نفسه غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه ( بخاری شریف، باب الوضوء ثلاثا ثلاثا ص ۱۳۲ نمبر ۱۵۹رابوداود شریف ، باب صفة وضوء النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ص ۲۶ نمبر ۱۰۸) اس حدیث میں کعبین کا لفظ ہے کہ ہر پاؤں میں دو ٹخنے دھوئے ، اور ہر پاؤں میں دو ٹخنے اوپر کے مختنے ہی ہیں اس لئے وہی مراد ہیں۔ (۲) رأيت أبا هريرة يتوضأ فغسل وجهه فاسبغ الوضوء ثم غسل يده اليمنى حتى اشرع في العضد ثم يده اليسرى حتى اشرع في العضد ثم مسح برأسه ثم غسل رجله اليمنى حتى اشرع في الساق ثم غسل رجله اليسرى حتي اشرع في الساق ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله الا الله يتوضا - (مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب اطالة الغرة والجميل فى الوضوء، ص ۱۲۱، نمبر
(65) Second: washing his hands with his elbows. (66) Third: washing his feet with his ankles. (67) Fourth: wiping part of the head. Translation: (65) The second fard is washing both hands including the elbows. Explanation: The elbows are included in washing the hands; its proof has passed from the verse and hadith. Proof: (1) From Jabir ibn Abdullah: The Messenger of Allah, when he performed wudu, would pour water over his elbows (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter on Wudu of the Prophet, vol. 1, p. 86, no. 268; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Including the Elbows in Wudu, vol. 1, p. 93, no. 25). This hadith shows that the elbows are included. (2) I said to 'Ata: 'Wash your faces and hands to the elbows' - is it to be washed? He said: Yes, no doubt about it. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, vol. 1, Chapter on Washing the Forearms, p. 5, no. 2). This athar shows that the elbows are definitely included. Translation: (66) The third fard is washing both feet including the ankles. Explanation: Washing both feet including the ankles is fard, and the ankle is included in washing. And what is meant is the upper ankle (the protruding bone), not the lower one. The verse and hadith for this have already passed. Proof: (1) The hadith of Humran (already cited) mentions 'to the ankles' (ka'bayn), and each foot has two ankles, which are the upper ones. (2) I saw Abu Hurairah performing wudu; he washed his face thoroughly, then his right hand until he reached the upper arm, then his left hand until the upper arm, then wiped his head, then washed his right foot until he reached the shin, then his left foot until the shin, then said: This is how I saw the Messenger of Allah performing wudu. (Sahih Muslim, Chapter on the Desirability of Extending the Forehead and Hands in Wudu, p. 121, no.)
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage covers the second, third, and fourth fard acts of wudu. For the second fard (washing hands to elbows), the author emphasizes that the elbows themselves must be washed, citing a hadith of Jabir and an athar from 'Ata. For the third fard (washing feet to ankles), the author specifies that the 'ankles' refer to the protruding bones on the sides of the foot (the medial and lateral malleoli), not the joint. The same hadith of Humran (using the word 'ka'bayn') is cited again, along with a hadith of Abu Hurairah showing washing up to the shin. For the fourth fard, the text only mentions 'wiping some of the head' (based on the corrected Arabic), with no further elaboration here. The earlier part of the passage in lesson 1 indicated that the minimum is a quarter of the head. The proofs for these acts rely on the general Quranic verse and specific narrations showing the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
كعب (ka'b): The ankle bone, specifically the protruding bone on each side of the foot. In wudu, both ankle bones must be washed.
مرفق (mirfaq): Elbow; must be washed in wudu.

Key Takeaway

Second Fard of Wudu: Hands Including Elbows
States the second fard of wudu with proof from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the second fard of wudu and explain the evidence that the elbows are included.

Core Idea
Washing the hands in wudu includes the elbows – the proof lies in the Prophet's practice.

In this lesson, we examine the second obligatory act of wudu: washing the hands along with the elbows. The Hanafi school maintains that 'to the elbows' in the Quranic verse includes the elbows themselves. We will look at the evidence from the Prophet's wudu and the statement of the tabi'i Ata.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is washing the hands including the elbows. The ruling is fard (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
Two pieces of evidence: a hadith from Jabir showing the Prophet poured water over his elbows, and an athar from Ata affirming the inclusion.
These are secondary evidence supporting the Quranic verse.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith directly shows the Prophet washing the elbows. The athar confirms this understanding. This indicates the elbows are part of the wash.
The specific phrase 'adara al-ma'a 'ala mafiqihi' is key.
4
Note any ikhtilaf
There is no disagreement within the Hanafi school on this point. Other schools agree on washing the elbows, though they may differ on the method.
5
Conclude the ruling
The evidence firmly supports that washing the hands includes the elbows. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
The ruling is fard 'ayn.

Section on Wudu (65) The second is washing his hands together with his elbows. Translation: (65) The second fard is washing both hands including the elbows. Explanation: In washing both hands, the elbows are included. Its proof has passed with the verse and hadith. Evidence: (1) From Jabir ibn Abdillah, he said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed wudu, he would pour water over his elbows. (Darqutni ...) This hadith shows that the elbows are included in washing. (2) I said to Ata: 'Then wash your faces and your hands up to the elbows.' Should he wash? He said: Yes, no doubt about it. Commentary
This passage presents the second obligatory act (fard) of wudu: washing the hands including the elbows. The author first states the ruling clearly: the hands must be washed together with the elbows. Then he provides evidence. The first evidence is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdillah, which shows that the Prophet (peace be upon him) poured water over his elbows during wudu, indicating that the elbows are included in the washing. The second evidence is a statement from Ata (a tabi'i), who affirmed that the elbows are washed based on the Quranic verse. Both proofs establish that the elbows are part of the hands for the purpose of wudu. The commentary emphasizes that the elbows are not separate but are included within the command to wash the hands. This is a standard Hanafi position, based on the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse 'to the elbows' which, according to Hanafi usul, includes the limit itself within the command.

Key Terms
مرفق (mirfaq): The elbow; the joint between the upper arm and forearm.

Third Fard of Wudu: Washing Feet Including Ankles
States the third obligatory act of wudu with proof that ankles are included.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the third fard of wudu, explain the Hanafi definition of ka'b, and apply the ghayah inclusion principle to justify that the ankles are included in the washing.

Core Idea
Washing the feet must include the upper ankle bones – the limit is part of the limited.

Washing the feet is one of the four obligatory acts (faraid) of wudu. But where exactly does the washing end? The Quran and hadith specify 'up to the ankles.' This lesson unpacks the Hanafi understanding that the ankles themselves must be washed, not just the foot below them. We will examine the textual evidence and the linguistic principle that governs this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon. It is washing the feet during wudu. The ruling is that it is fard (obligatory) and that the ankles must be included.
The Hanafi school counts this as one of the four faraid of wudu.
2
Locate the primary hadith proof
Find the hadith from Uthman (radiyallahu anhu) that describes the Prophet's wudu. The phrase 'ghasala rijlayhi ila al-ka'bain' explicitly shows washing up to the ankles.
The same hadith is reported by Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the secondary hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Hurairah shows washing the feet up to the shin, indicating that the ankle is part of the foot, just as the elbow is part of the arm.
This reinforces the inclusion of the ankle in the washing command.
4
Understand the linguistic principle (ghayah)
The passage explains a usul al-fiqh principle: when a limit (ghayah) and the limited (mighyah) share the same genus, the limit is included in the command. Since the foot and ankle are of the same genus (both part of the leg), the ankle is included.
Contrast with the fast where night (different genus) is excluded from the fasting period.
5
Note the Hanafi definition of ka'b
The Hanafi school defines ka'b as the upper protruding ankle bones (one on each side). This is the limit to be washed.
Other schools define it differently, leading to practical differences in wudu.

(٦٦) والثالث غسل رجليه مع كعبيه . ترجمه : (۶۶) تیسرا فرض دونوں پاؤں کو ٹخنوں سمیت دھونا ہے۔ تشریح : دونوں پاؤں کو ٹخنوں سمیت دھونا فرض ہے، اور ٹخنہ دھونے میں شامل ہے، اور اس ٹخنے سے اوپر والا ٹخنہ مراد ہے نیچے والا ٹخنہ مراد نہیں ہے۔ اس کے لئے بھی آیت اور حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) ان حمران مولى عثمان اخبره انه رأى عثمان بن عفان دعا باناء ، فافرغ على كفيه ثلاث مرار فغسلهما ، ثم ادخل يمينه فى الاناء فمضمض واستنثر ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا و يديه الى المرفقين ثلاث مرار صلى الله ،ثم مسح برأسه ،ثم غسل رجليه ثلاث مرار الى الكعبين ، ثم قال : قال رسول الله علم : من توضأ نحو وضوئى هذا ثم صلى ركعتين لا يحدث فيهما نفسه غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه ( بخاری شریف، باب الوضوء ثلاثا ثلاثا ص ۱۳۲ نمبر ۱۵۹رابوداود شریف ، باب صفة وضوء النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ، ص ۲۶ نمبر ۱۰۸) اس حدیث میں کعبین کا لفظ ہے کہ ہر پاؤں میں دو ٹخنے دھوئے ، اور ہر پاؤں میں دو ٹخنے اوپر کے مختنے ہی ہیں اس لئے وہی مراد ہیں۔ (۲) رأيت أبا هريرة يتوضأ فغسل وجهه فاسبغ الوضوء ثم غسل يده اليمنى حتى اشرع في العضد ثم يده اليسرى حتى اشرع في العضد ثم مسح برأسه ثم غسل رجله اليمنى حتى اشرع في الساق ثم غسل رجله اليسرى حتي اشرع في الساق ثم قال هكذا رأيت رسول الله الا الله يتوضا - (مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب اطالة الغرة وال الجميل فى الوضوء، ص ۱۲۱، نمبر ۵۷۹/۲۴۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہاتھ کو باز و تک دھویا ، اور پاؤں کو پنڈلی تک دھویا، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کہنی ہاتھ میں شامل ہے اور ٹخنے پاؤں میں شامل ہیں ۔ (۳) انگلی سے لیکر مونڈھے تک کو ہاتھ کہتے ہیں اس لئے اگر آیت میں کہنیوں کی قید نہ لگاتے تو مونڈھے تک دھونا فرض ہوتا اس لئے کہنیوں تک دھونے کے لئے کہا تو کہنیوں سے آگے ساقط ہو گیا۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو عضو آگے کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے آئے وہ اس حکم میں داخل ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہنی دھونے کے حکم میں داخل رہے گی۔ اس طرح رجل (پاؤں ) ران تک کو کہتے ہیں۔ ٹخنہ تک کی قید لگا کر ٹخنہ سے اوپر کو ساقط کیا۔ لیکن خود خنہ دھونے کے حکم میں داخل رہے گا۔ اصول : جنس ایک ہو تو غایت مغیا میں داخل ہوتا ہے ۔۲ جنس دو ہوں تو غایت مغیاء میں داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسے روزے میں رات داخل نہیں۔ لغت : کعب : ابھری ہوئی چیز ٹخنہ ۔
(66) The third is washing his feet together with his ankles. Translation: (66) The third fard is washing both feet including the ankles. Explanation: Washing both feet including the ankles is fard, and the ankle is included in the wash, and here the upper ankle is meant, not the lower ankle. For this also, the verse and hadith have passed. Evidence: (1) That Humran, the client of Uthman, informed him that he saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel, and he poured water on his hands three times and washed them, then he put his right hand into the vessel and rinsed his mouth and nose, then washed his face three times, and his hands up to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times up to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without speaking to himself, his previous sins are forgiven. (Bukhari, Book of Wudu chapter; Abu Dawud...) In this hadith is the word 'ka'bain' that both feet have two ankles washed, and each foot has two upper ankles, so that is what is meant. (2) I saw Abu Hurairah perform wudu; he washed his face and completed the wudu, then washed his right hand until he went into the upper arm, then his left hand until he went into the upper arm, then wiped his head, then washed his right foot until he went into the shin, then washed his left foot until he went into the shin, then said: Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) perform wudu. (Muslim, Book of Wudu...) In this hadith it mentions that he washed the hands up to the upper arm and the feet up to the shin, showing that the elbow is included in the hand and the ankles are included in the feet. (3) The finger to the shoulder is called the hand; so if the verse had not specified the limit of the elbows, washing up to the shoulder would be fard. So when it said up to the elbows, beyond the elbows is dropped. And the rule is: whatever comes to drop something beyond is included in that ruling. Therefore, the elbow remains included in the command to wash. Similarly, the foot (leg) from toe to thigh is called the leg; the limit of the ankle was set to drop above the ankle, but the ankle itself remains included in the command to wash. Principle: If the genus is one, the limit is included in the limited; if the genus is two, the limit is not included in the limited, like the night is not included in the fast. Lexicon: Ka'b: protruding thing, ankle.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage establishes the third fard of wudu: washing the feet including the ankles. The author clarifies that 'ankle' here refers to the upper ankle (the protruding bone), not the lower. He provides multiple proofs. First, a well-known hadith from Uthman (radiyallahu anhu) describing the Prophet's wudu, which includes washing the feet up to the ankles. This shows that washing includes the ankles. Second, a hadith from Abu Hurairah (radiyallahu anhu) where he washed his feet up to the shin, indicating that the ankle is part of the foot. Third, a rational proof based on linguistic usage: the term 'hand' includes the arm to the shoulder, but the Quranic specification 'to the elbows' excludes the upper arm while including the elbows themselves. The same principle applies to the feet: the term 'foot' includes the leg to the thigh, but the verse limits it to the ankles, thereby excluding the shin and thigh but including the ankles. The author then states the usul principle: when the limit (ghayah) and the limited (mighyah) share the same genus, the limit is included; when they are of different genera, the limit is excluded. This principle is used to justify that the elbows and ankles are included in the wash. The lexical note defines 'ka'b' as the protruding ankle bone.

Key Terms
كعب (ka'b): The protruding ankle bone at the base of the lower leg.
غاية (ghayah): Limit, endpoint, boundary. In usul al-fiqh, the term up to which a ruling applies.
مغيا (mighyah): That which is limited by the ghayah; the object of the command that has a boundary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Washing the feet in wudu must include the upper ankle bones; the Hanafi school proves this through the Prophet's practice and the usul principle of ghayah inclusion.

The Fourth Fard of Wudu: Wiping a Quarter of the Head
States the fourth fard with two hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum obligatory amount of head wiping in wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Wiping a quarter of the head is fard; the Prophet's wiping his forelock proves the minimum.

Wudu has four obligatory acts (fara'id). The fourth is wiping a part of the head. The Hanafi school uniquely specifies that the obligatory amount is one quarter of the head, based on clear prophetic practice. This lesson examines the proof and clarifies that wiping the entire head is a recommended sunnah, not a requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth fard
Locate in the passage the statement that the fourth fard of wudu is wiping part of the head. Note that the Arabic term 'masḥ baʿḍ al-ra's' is used.
The OCR corruption in the Arabic heading is ignored; the intended meaning is clear.
2
Examine the first hadith proof
Read the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah where the Prophet wiped his forelock (nāṣiyah). Understand that the forelock is approximately one quarter of the head.
The phrase 'masaḥa bi nāṣiyatihi' is the key evidence.
3
Examine the second hadith proof
Read the hadith where the Prophet wiped the front of his head (muqaddam ra'sih). This further supports that the entire head is not required.
Both hadith are from authentic collections (Muslim, Abu Dawud).
4
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Conclude that the minimum fard is a quarter of the head, based on the forelock measurement. Understand that wiping the whole head is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard.
Contrast with the Shafi'i position that any part suffices, but Hanafis require a specific measurable portion.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, ensure that at least a quarter of the head is wiped during wudu. The quarter can be any contiguous area, but the forelock is the standard example.
If less than a quarter is wiped, wudu is invalid.

(۶۷) والرابع مسح بعض الـعـركـ ثم شبك لحيته بأصابعه من تحتها - (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء تخلیل اللحیة، ص ۶۳ نمبر ۴۳۲) اس حديث میں ہے کہ دونوں گالوں کو رگڑتے تھے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں گال وضو میں داخل ہیں۔ لغت : مبداً: شروع۔ جبہتہ : پیشانی۔ الذقن تھوڑی ۔ شحمہ کان کی لو، چر بی۔اذ نین: اذن کی تنثنیہ ہے، کان۔ ترجمه : (۶۷) اور چوتھا فرض چوتھائی سر کا مسح کرنا ہے۔ وجه : (ا) عن عروة بن المغيرة بن شعبة ، عن ابيه قال : تخلف رسول الله الا الله و تخلفت معه، فلما قضى حاجته ..... ومسح بناصيته ، و على العمامة ، و على خفيه ، (مسلم شریف، باب المسح على الناصية ، والعمامة، ص۱۳۴ نمبر ۱۳۳/۲۷۴، ابوداود شریف باب المسح علی الخفین ہی ۲ نمبر ۱۵۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پیشانی کے قریب جو بال ہے آپ نے اس پس فرمایا اوروہ چوتھائی سر کی مقدار ہے اسلئے چوتھائی سر پرسی کرنا فرض ہوگا۔ (۲) عن ابن المغيرة عن اب : ان نبی الله الله مسح على الخفين ، و مقدم رأسه ، و على عمامته. (مسلم شریف، باب المسح على الناصية والعمامة ، ص ۱۳۴، نمبر ۶۳۴/۲۷۴ را بود و دشریف، باب المسیح علی العمامۃ ، ص ۲۲، نمبر ۱۴۷) جب سر کے صرف اگلے حصے پر مسح کیا تو پتہ یہ چلا کہ پورے سر کا مسح کرنا فرض نہیں ہے، بلکہ مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ پورے سر کا مسح فرض ہوتا تو صرف پیشانی کی مقدار یا اگلے حصے پر مسح کرنا کافی نہیں ہوتا۔ اور پیشانی کی مقدار چوتھائی سر ہوتا ہے اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک چوتھائی سر کا مسح کرنا فرض ہے۔ اور پورے سر پر مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔
(67) The fourth is wiping part of the head, then he combed his beard with his fingers from below. (Ibn Majah, Chapter on Coming to the Beard...) In this hadith it mentions that he would rub both cheeks, from which it is known that both cheeks are included in wudu. Lexicon: Mubda': beginning; jabhatah: forehead; al-dhaqan: chin; shahmah: earlobe, fat; udhnain: dual of udhun, ears. Translation: (67) And the fourth fard is wiping a quarter of the head. Evidence: (1) From Urwah ibn al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, from his father, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) lagged behind and I lagged behind with him. When he finished his need... and he wiped his forelock, and over his turban, and over his khuffs. (Muslim, Book of Wiping over the Forelock and Turban; Abu Dawud...) From this hadith it is known that he wiped the hair near the forehead, and that is the amount of a quarter of the head, so wiping a quarter of the head becomes fard. (2) From Ibn al-Mughirah from his father: The Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped over his khuffs, and the front of his head, and over his turban. (Muslim, Book...) When he wiped only the front part of the head, it became clear that wiping the entire head is not fard, but mustahabb. Because if wiping the entire head were fard, then wiping only the amount of the forehead or the front part would not suffice. And the amount of the forehead is a quarter of the head, so according to the Hanafis, wiping a quarter of the head is fard, and wiping the entire head is sunnah.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth fard of wudu: wiping a quarter of the head. The Arabic heading has a corruption but likely reads 'wiping part of the head'. The text includes a hadith about combing the beard and rubbing cheeks, which seems to be a separate proof for including the cheeks in face washing, but it is placed here possibly due to OCR misordering. The intended focus is on head wiping. The author provides two key hadith proofs. In the first, the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped his forelock (nasiyah), which is the hair on the front of the head, approximately a quarter. This indicates that wiping a quarter of the head is sufficient. In the second hadith, the Prophet wiped the front of his head (muqaddam ra'sih), again indicating that the whole head is not required. The author concludes that wiping the entire head is sunnah, but the obligatory minimum is a quarter. This is a distinct Hanafi position; other schools like Shafi'i require wiping at least part of the head, but Hanafis specify a quarter as the minimum based on these narrations. The lexical glossary preceding the translation defines terms related to the face, indicating that the passage originally included definitions for face-related terms, but it is placed here.

Key Terms
مسح (mash): To wipe; passing wet hand over a body part without flowing water.
الناصية (al-nasiyah): The forelock; the front part of the hair on the head.

Cause and Ruling of Wudu
Defines the cause and rulings of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the cause (sabab) of wudu and distinguish its worldly and otherworldly rulings.

Core Idea
Wudu is a means to make permissible what is otherwise prohibited – its cause is the need for purification.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational definition of wudu in Hanafi fiqh: what triggers it and what it achieves. Understanding the cause (sabab) versus the ruling (hukm) is crucial for grasping why wudu becomes obligatory in specific contexts. The passage breaks down wudu into two dimensions: a worldly legal effect and an otherworldly spiritual reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being defined
The passage defines wudu. Note that wudu is a ritual purification act, not an end in itself.
2
Extract the cause (sabab)
The cause is 'to make permissible what is not permissible without it'. This is the trigger that necessitates wudu when one intends an act requiring purification.
In Hanafi usul, sabab is what necessitates the ruling when present.
3
Distinguish the two rulings
Worldly ruling: legal permissibility of acts like prayer. Otherworldly ruling: reward in the afterlife. These are two distinct effects of the same act.
4
Apply to a concrete example
If a Muslim wants to pray Fajr, prayer is not permissible without wudu. Thus, the need to pray becomes the cause that makes wudu obligatory. After wudu, prayer becomes permissible (worldly effect), and the wudu itself earns reward (otherworldly effect).
This illustrates the difference between sabab and shart: sabab triggers obligation, shart is a condition for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۶۸) وضو کا سبب جو چیز وضو کے بغیر حلال نہیں ہے اس کو حلال کرنا ہے، اور یہ اس کا دنیوی حکم ہے اور وضو کا اخری حکم آخرت میں ثواب حاصل کرنا ہے۔ تشریح : وضو کا سبب یہ ہے کہ جو چیز وضو کے بغیر حلال نہیں ہے، مثلا نماز بغیر وضو کے حلال نہیں ہے تو وضو کر نے کے بعد نماز حلال ہو جائے گی یہ اس کا دنیوی حکم ہے اور وضو کا اُخروی حکم یہ ہے کہ وضو سے ثواب حاصل ہوگا۔
Translation: (68) The cause of wudu is to make permissible what is not permissible without it, and this is its worldly ruling, and the otherworldly ruling of wudu is to attain reward in the afterlife. Explanation: The cause of wudu is that a thing that is not permissible without wudu, for example, prayer is not permissible without wudu, so after performing wudu, prayer becomes permissible. This is its worldly ruling, and the otherworldly ruling of wudu is that reward will be attained from it.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage explains the cause (sabab) of wudu and its two rulings: worldly and otherworldly. The cause of wudu is the need to perform acts that require purification, such as prayer, which are not permissible without it. Thus, wudu is the means to make these acts permissible, which is its worldly effect. The otherworldly ruling is that performing wudu brings reward in the afterlife. This is a general statement in Hanafi fiqh, defining wudu as a cause (sabab) for the permissibility of ritual acts, as opposed to being a condition (shart) per se. The worldly ruling is legal permissibility, and the otherworldly is spiritual reward.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): Cause; what necessitates the ruling when it occurs. Here, the need to make permissible an act that requires purification is the sabab for wudu.

C) To attain purity of the soul
D) To beautify oneself

Key Takeaway
Wudu's cause is the need to make permissible acts like salah; its worldly effect is legal permissibility and its otherworldly effect is reward.

The Fourth Fard of Wudu: Wiping a Quarter of the Head
States the fourth fard of wudu and proves it with hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for wiping the head in wudu and derive it from the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Wiping only a quarter of the head is obligatory; the entire head is sunnah.

In this lesson, we examine the fourth fard of wudu according to the Hanafi school: wiping a quarter of the head. The matn states this ruling, and the sharh provides two hadiths demonstrating that the Prophet (ﷺ) wiped only his forelock and the front of his head. You will learn how the Hanafis derive the quarter obligation from these narrations and why the Shafi'i position differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The lesson states that the fourth fard is wiping a quarter of the head (rub' ra's). This is the obligatory minimum.
The act is mash (wiping) on the head.
2
Locate the Hadith Evidence
Two hadiths are cited: one mentioning the forelock (nasiyah) and another mentioning the front of the head (muqaddam ra's). Both are from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
These are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for fard in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet wiped only a part of his head, indicating that a fraction suffices. The forelock is approximately a quarter of the head.
The second hadith specifies the front part, further supporting that the entire head is not required.
4
Apply the Usuli Principle of Ghayah
The text discusses the rule that when a limit (ghayah) is set, the limit itself is included in the ruling if the genus is one. Here, the quarter is included as part of the head.
This principle is also applied to the elbows and ankles in wudu.
5
Compare with Opposing School
Shafi'is require wiping the entire head based on a different interpretation of the Quranic command. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ربع رأسه . (۲۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ہاتھ کو بازو تک دھویا ، اور پاؤں کو پنڈلی تک دھویا، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کہنی ہاتھ میں شامل ہے اور ٹخنے پاؤں میں شامل ہیں ۔ (۳) انگلی سے لیکر مونڈھے تک کو ہاتھ کہتے ہیں اس لئے اگر آیت میں کہنیوں کی قید نہ لگاتے تو مونڈھے تک دھونا فرض ہوتا اس لئے کہنیوں تک دھونے کے لئے کہا تو کہنیوں سے آگے ساقط ہو گیا۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو عضو آگے کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے آئے وہ اس حکم میں داخل ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہنی دھونے کے حکم میں داخل رہے گی۔ اس طرح رجل (پاؤں ) ران تک کو کہتے ہیں۔ ٹخنہ تک کی قید لگا کر ٹخنہ سے اوپر کو ساقط کیا۔ لیکن خود خنہ دھونے کے حکم میں داخل رہے گا۔ اصول : جنس ایک ہو تو غایت مغیا میں داخل ہوتا ہے ۔۲ جنس دو ہوں تو غایت مغیاء میں داخل نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسے روزے میں رات داخل نہیں۔ لغت : کعب : ابھری ہوئی چیز ٹخنہ ۔ ترجمه : (۶۷) اور چوتھا فرض چوتھائی سر کا مسح کرنا ہے۔ وجه : (ا) عن عروة بن المغيرة بن شعبة ، عن ابيه قال : تخلف رسول الله الا الله و تخلفت معه، فلما قضى حاجته ..... ومسح بناصيته ، و على العمامة ، و على خفيه ، (مسلم شریف، باب المسح على الناصية ، والعمامة، ص۱۳۴ نمبر ۱۳۳/۲۷۴، ابوداود شریف باب المسح علی الخفین ہی ۲ نمبر ۱۵۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ پیشانی کے قریب جو بال ہے آپ نے اس پس فرمایا اوروہ چوتھائی سر کی مقدار ہے اسلئے چوتھائی سر پرسی کرنا فرض ہوگا۔ (۲) عن ابن المغيرة عن اب : ان نبی الله الله مسح على الخفين ، و مقدم رأسه ، و على عمامته. (مسلم شریف، باب المسح على الناصية والعمامة ، ص ۱۳۴، نمبر ۶۳۴/۲۷۴ را بود و دشریف، باب المسیح علی العمامۃ ، ص ۲۲، نمبر ۱۴۷) جب سر کے صرف اگلے حصے پر مسح کیا تو پتہ یہ چلا کہ پورے سر کا مسح کرنا فرض نہیں ہے، بلکہ مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ پورے سر کا مسح فرض ہوتا تو صرف پیشانی کی مقدار یا اگلے حصے پر مسح کرنا کافی نہیں ہوتا۔ اور پیشانی کی مقدار چوتھائی سر ہوتا ہے اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک چوتھائی سر کا مسح کرنا فرض ہے۔ اور پورے سر پر مسح کرنا سنت ہے۔
A quarter of his head. (28) This hadith mentions that he washed his hands up to the forearm and his feet up to the shin, from which it is understood that the elbow is included in the hand and the ankle is included in the foot. (3) From the fingertips to the shoulder is called the hand; therefore if the verse had not specified the elbows, washing up to the shoulder would be obligatory. Since it said to wash up to the elbows, what is beyond the elbows is excluded. And the rule is that the part that comes to exclude further parts is itself included in the ruling. Thus the elbow remains included in the ruling of washing. Similarly, the foot is called from the toe to the thigh. By specifying up to the ankle, what is above the ankle is excluded, but the ankle itself remains included. Principle: If the genus is one, then the limit is included in the limited; if genus is two, then the limit is not included. Like night is not included in fasting. Lexicon: ka'b: a protruding thing, the ankle. Translation: (67) The fourth fard is to wipe a quarter of the head. Proof: (1) From 'Urwa ibn al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba from his father: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) lagged behind... and he wiped his forelock, his turban, and his leather socks.' (Muslim, no. 133/274; Abu Dawud, no. 150). From this hadith it is understood that he wiped the hair near the forehead, which is a quarter of the head, so wiping a quarter of the head is fard. (2) From Ibn al-Mughira from his father: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) wiped his leather socks, the front of his head, and his turban.' (Muslim, no. 134/274; Abu Dawud, no. 147). When he only wiped the front part of the head, it shows that wiping the entire head is not fard, but mustahabb. Because if wiping the entire head were fard, then wiping only the forehead or front part would not suffice. And the forehead's portion is a quarter of the head, so according to the Hanafis, wiping a quarter of the head is fard, and wiping the entire head is sunnah.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil). The matn states the fourth fard of wudu: wiping a quarter of the head. The sharh first provides a linguistic and legal discussion about the inclusion of the limit (ghayah) in the limited (mughaya), using the example of the hands and feet to illustrate the principle. It explains that when Allah commanded washing the hands to the elbows, the elbow is included, and similarly for the feet to the ankles. This principle applies to the head as well. Then it provides the exact ruling: wiping a quarter of the head is fard. The proof (wajh) is from two hadiths: one where the Prophet wiped his forelock (nasiyah) and another where he wiped the front part of his head (muqaddam ra'sih). These show that the entire head is not required; the minimum is a quarter. The Hanafi position is that wiping a quarter is fard, and wiping the entire head is sunnah. This differs from other schools that require wiping the entire head. The text also defines 'ka'b' as ankle bone, and outlines the usuli principle regarding ghayah.

Key Terms
ربع (rub'): One quarter of an organ; the minimum amount that must be wiped in wudu according to Hanafis.
مسح (mash): Wiping the head or leather socks with wet hands; a main action in wudu.
ناصية (nasiyah): The forelock or front part of the head; in the hadith, the Prophet wiped this portion.
كعب (ka'b): The protruding ankle bone; the limit of washing the feet in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A quarter of the head
C) The forelock only
D) Any part of the head

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires wiping a quarter of the head as fard; wiping the entire head is sunnah, based on the Prophet's action of wiping his forelock.

Taharah — Purification

6 min
The Cause (Sabab) of Wudu and Its Two Rulings
Defines the cause of wudu and its two rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the sabab of wudu, distinguish its worldly and otherworldly rulings, and cite the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
Wudu's cause is to permit acts like prayer; its worldly effect is permissibility, its otherworldly effect is reward.

This lesson clarifies what wudu actually does. Many think wudu is only for physical cleanliness or that its purpose is to remove sin. While wudu does have spiritual benefits, its primary legal function (sabab) is to make permissible acts that require purity, such as salah and tawaf. The author distinguishes between the worldly legal effect (istibahah) and the otherworldly reward (thawab), and provides hadith evidence for both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term sabab
The word 'sabab' here means the instrumental cause. Wudu is the means by which acts that are otherwise prohibited (like prayer without purification) become permissible. Distinguish this from the cause of obligation (e.g., time for salah).
In Hanafi usul, sabab is a manifest sign, but here it is used in a simpler sense.
2
Distinguish worldly and otherworldly rulings
The worldly ruling (hukm dunawi) is istibahah—making permissible what was impermissible. The otherworldly ruling (hukm ukhrawi) is reward (thawab) from Allah. Note that these two rulings are separate but both result from the same act of wudu.
3
Analyze the hadith for the worldly ruling
The hadith 'لا تقبل صلاة بغير طهور' proves that purification is a necessary condition for prayer's acceptance. The negation of acceptance indicates that prayer without wudu is invalid, thus establishing the worldly effect of wudu.
This hadith is a sunnah ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah) for Hanafis.
4
Analyze the hadith for the otherworldly ruling
The second hadith describes the expiation of sins through wudu. This establishes the reward (thawab) in the Hereafter. Understand that this reward is a spiritual benefit beyond the legal permissibility.
The reward is not the sabab itself but a consequence.
5
Apply the distinction to daily practice
When performing wudu, keep in mind both effects: the act makes your salah valid (worldly) and also earns you reward (otherworldly). This dual perspective enriches the intention.

وسببه استباحة ما لا يحل الا به وهو حكمه الدنيوى وحكمه الأخروى الثواب في الآخرة . ترجمه : (۶۸) وضو کا سبب جو چیز وضو کے بغیر حلال نہیں ہے اس کو حلال کرنا ہے، اور یہ اس کا دنیوی حکم ہے اور وضو کا اخری حکم آخرت میں ثواب حاصل کرنا ہے۔ تشریح : وضو کا سبب یہ ہے کہ جو چیز وضو کے بغیر حلال نہیں ہے، مثلا نماز بغیر وضو کے حلال نہیں ہے تو وضو کر نے کے بعد نماز حلال ہو جائے گی یہ اس کا دنیوی حکم ہے اور وضو کا اُخروی حکم یہ ہے کہ وضو سے ثواب حاصل ہوگا۔ وجه : ( ا ) دخل عبد الله ابن عمر على ابن عامر يعوده و هو مريض فقال الا تدعو الله لي يا ابن عمر ؟ قال اني سمعت رسول الله الله يقول : لا تقبل صلوة بغير طهور ولا صدقة من غلول ( مسلم شريف، باب وجوب الطهارة للصلاة ،ص۱۱۴، نمبر ۵۳۵/۲۲۴/ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء لا تقبل صلوۃ بغیر طہور ،ص 1 نمبرا) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بغیر وضو کے نماز نہیں ہوتی۔ (۲) اور اُخروی اعتبار سے ثواب اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله اذا توضأ العبد المسلم او المؤمن فغسل وجهه خرجت من وجهه كل خطيئة نظر اليها بعينه مع الماء ، او مع آخر قطر الماء او نحو هذا ـ و اذا غسل يديه خرجت من يديه كل خطيئه بطشها يداه مع الماء او مع آخر قطر الماء ، حتى يخرج نقيا من الذنوب - ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی فضل الطهو ر ص ۲، نمبر ۲) اس حدیث میں وضو کا ثواب بیان کیا گیا ہے۔
And its cause is to make permissible that which is not permissible without it. It is its worldly ruling, and its otherworldly ruling is reward in the Hereafter. Translation: (68) The cause of wudu is to make permissible that which is not permissible without wudu, for example, prayer is not permissible without wudu, so after performing wudu, prayer becomes permissible. This is its worldly ruling. The otherworldly ruling of wudu is that one obtains reward in the Hereafter. Explanation: The cause of wudu is that which is not permissible without it; such as prayer is not permissible without wudu; after wudu, prayer becomes permissible. This is its worldly ruling. The otherworldly ruling is that reward is obtained. Proof: (1) 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar visited Ibn 'Amir who was sick and said: 'Will you not supplicate for me, O Ibn 'Umar?' He replied: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Prayer is not accepted without purification, nor is charity from ill-gotten gains.' (Muslim, no. 535/224; Tirmidhi). This hadith states that prayer is not valid without wudu. (2) Regarding the otherworldly reward, the Prophet said: 'When a Muslim slave (or believer) performs wudu and washes his face, every sin that he looked at with his eyes comes out with the water (or with the last drop of water). When he washes his hands, every sin that his hands committed comes out with the water... until he emerges purified from sins.' (Tirmidhi, no. 2). This hadith explains the reward of wudu.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This is a definition-ruling passage. It defines the sabab (cause) of wudu and distinguishes between its worldly (dunawi) and otherworldly (ukhrawi) rulings. The sabab is not the reason for obligation (that is prayer time) but rather the effect: wudu makes permissible acts that are otherwise impermissible without it, like prayer and tawaf. The worldly ruling is istibahah (making permissible), while the otherworldly ruling is thawaab (reward). The proof (wajh) provides two hadith: one establishing the worldly ruling (prayer without purification is not accepted) and one on the reward. Note that the sabab mentioned here is not the cause of obligation (which is aql, bulugh, Islam as in the next lesson) but the instrumental cause.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause or means; here it means that wudu is the means to make permissible acts that require purity.
حكم دنيوي (hukm dunawi): The worldly legal effect of wudu: it makes permissible what was impermissible.
حكم أخروي (hukm ukhrawi): The otherworldly effect: reward (thawab) for performing wudu.
استباحة (istibahah): Making something permissible; the result of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the worldly ruling (hukm dunawi) of wudu according to this passage?
A) It physically cleanses the body
B) It makes permissible acts that require purity
C) It cancels sins
D) It is a condition for entering the mosque

Key Takeaway
Wudu's sabab is to make permissible acts that require purity; its worldly effect is istibahah, and its otherworldly effect is reward.
