Conditions for the Obligation of Wudu: Intellect, Puberty, Islam
States the three conditions for wudu to be obligatory and proves each

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the obligation of wudu and provide a proof for each.

Core Idea
Wudu is obligatory only upon the sane, mature Muslim; the insane, child, and disbeliever are not required to perform it.

This lesson examines the conditions (shurut) that make wudu legally obligatory (wajib). Unlike conditions for validity, these shurut wujub determine who is addressed by the command to perform wudu. The Hanafi tradition holds that only a person who is sane, has reached puberty, and is Muslim is obligated. We will explore each condition and its evidence from the Quran, Sunna, and athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Wudu becomes wajib when three conditions are met. First, identify that we are dealing with the obligation (wujub) of wudu, not its validity.
Distinguish shart wujub from shart sihha.
2
Condition 1: Sanity (aql)
The hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' proves that the insane are not held accountable; thus wudu is not obligatory on them.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.
3
Condition 2: Puberty (bulugh)
The same hadith covers the child until he reaches puberty; a child below puberty has no legal responsibility.
Also supported by the athar of Ibn Abbas regarding zakat.
4
Condition 3: Islam
The Quranic verse about those who believe and establish prayer indicates that Islam is a prerequisite for the obligation of prayer, hence for wudu.
The verse is from Surah al-Naml or al-Anfal.
5
Application of the conditions
If any condition is missing, wudu is not wajib but may still be valid. For example, a child who performs wudu and prays has a valid prayer.
The same applies to the insane and the disbeliever according to the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط وجوبه العقل والبلوغ والاسلام . ترجمه : (۶۹) وضو واجب ہونے کی شرط عاقل، بالغ ، اور مسلمان ہونا ہے۔ تشريح : وضو واجب ہونے کی یہاں ۸ شرطیں بیان کی جارہی ہیں، ان میں سے تین یہ ہیں کہ آدمی [1] عاقل ہو [۲] بالغ ہو، [۳] اور مسلمان ہوتب وضو واجب ہوتا ہے، اگر آدمی عاقل نہیں ہے بلکہ مجنون ہے تو اس پر نہ نماز واجب ہے ، اور نہ وضو واجب ہے، ویسے وضو کر کے نماز پڑھ لے تو نماز ہو جائے گی، لیکن اس پر واجب نہیں ہے، اسی طرح اگر بالغ نہیں ہے بچہ ہے تو اس پر نہ نماز واجب ہے اور نہ اس پر وضو واجب ہے۔ آدمی مسلمان نہ ہو کا فر ہو تو نہ اس پر نماز واجب ہے اور نہ اس پر وضو واجب ہے۔ ہر ایک کی دلیل یہ ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عاقل ہو اور بالغ ہو تب وضو واجب ہو گا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عـلـى عن النبي الله قال رفع القلم عن ثلثة عن النائم حتى يستيقظ وعن الصبى حتى يحتلم وعن المجنون حتى يعقل . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في المجنون يسرق او یصیب حدا، ج ثانی ص ۲۵۶ کتاب الحدود نمبر ۴۴۰۳ رابن ماجه شریف ، باب طلاق المعتوه والصغير والنائم ، کتاب الطلاق ص ۲۹۲، نمبر ۲۰۴۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے ، اور مجنون کے اوپر کوئی ذمہ داری نہیں ہے تو وضو بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا ۔(۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال : لا يجب على مال الصغير زكاة حتى تجب عليه الصلاة (دارقطنی، باب استقراض الوصی من مال الیتیم ، ج ثانی ہیں ۹۷، نمبر ۱۹۶۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بچے پر نہ مال کی زکوۃ ہے اور نہ وضو ہے۔ (۳) اور مسلمان ہو اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ الذین يقيمون الصلوة ويؤتون الزكوة و هم بالآخرة هم يوقنون ( آیت ۳ ، سورۃ النمل (۲۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ وہ آخرت پر یقین رکھتا ہو یعنی مسلمان ہو تب اس پر نماز ہے اور تب ہی وضو ہے
And the condition of its obligation is intellect, puberty, and Islam. Translation: (69) The condition for wudu to be obligatory is that one be sane, mature, and Muslim. Explanation: Here eight conditions for the obligation of wudu are being explained; three of them are: (1) sane, (2) mature, (3) Muslim. Then wudu is obligatory. If a person is not sane but insane, then neither prayer is obligatory on him nor wudu. However, if he performs wudu and prays, the prayer will be valid, but it is not obligatory. Similarly, if he is not mature but a child, then neither prayer nor wudu is obligatory. If a person is not Muslim but a disbeliever, then neither prayer nor wudu is obligatory. The proof for each: (1) For sanity and maturity, the hadith: 'Ali narrated from the Prophet (ﷺ) said: The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he regains sanity.' (Abu Dawud, no. 4403; Ibn Majah, no. 2042). This shows that the child and the insane have no responsibility, so wudu is not obligatory on them. (2) An athar from Ibn 'Abbas: 'Zakat is not obligatory on the wealth of a minor until prayer becomes obligatory on him.' (Darqutni). This shows that the child has neither zakat nor wudu. (3) For Islam, the verse: 'Those who believe in the unseen, establish prayer, and spend from what We have provided them.' (Surah al-Naml, verse 3? Actually the text says 'آیت ۳ ، سورۃ النمل (۲۷)' but that is incorrect; the correct verse is Al-Anfal 8:3 or similar. The text likely refers to a verse about believers establishing prayer. The intended meaning is that Islam is a prerequisite.) The verse indicates that belief (Islam) is a prerequisite for the obligation of prayer, and hence for wudu.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof (hukm wa dalil). The matn states the conditions (shurut) for the obligation (wujub) of wudu. These are technical conditions: intellect (aql), puberty (bulugh), and Islam. The sharh clarifies that these are three of eight conditions for wujub. It explains that these are conditions for the act being wajib (obligatory); if they are absent, there is no sin in leaving wudu, but if they perform it, it is valid. The proofs: for intellect and puberty, the hadith 'pen is lifted' (raf'a al-qalam) indicating that children and insane are not held accountable. For Islam, the Quranic verse stating that only the God-conscious (believers) are the ones who pray and pay zakat. Note that the text says 'shart wujubihi' (condition of its obligation), meaning that without these conditions, wudu is not legally required. This is a key distinction from conditions of validity (shurut al-sihha).

Key Terms
شرط وجوب (shart wujub): A condition for the act to be legally required (wajib); if absent, the act is not obligatory but may still be valid.
عقل (aql): Sanity or intellect; necessary for legal obligation.
بلوغ (bulugh): Puberty; the age of legal responsibility.
رفع القلم (raf' al-qalam): The lifting of the pen (recording of deeds) from certain individuals; meaning they are not held accountable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Being in a state of minor impurity (hadath)
B) Sanity (aql)
C) Being in the mosque
D) Having water available

Key Takeaway
Wudu is only obligatory upon the sane, mature Muslim; others are not required to perform it, but if they do, it is valid.

Three Conditions for Wudu Obligation: Sanity, Puberty, Islam
States three conditions for wudu obligation with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for wudu obligation and explain the proof for each from the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wudu is obligatory only on the sane, adult Muslim; for others it is not required.

This lesson identifies the three conditions that must be present for wudu to be obligatory in the Hanafi school. It also clarifies that obligation does not equal validity: an insane person or child may perform wudu and it will be valid, but it is not required of them. The proofs include the hadith of 'the pen is lifted' and a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
Read the text to find the three conditions for wudu obligation: sanity (al-aql), puberty (al-bulugh), and Islam (al-islam).
2
Understand the legal effect
If any condition is absent, wudu is not obligatory. However, if performed, it is valid.
Distinguish between obligation (wujub) and validity (sihha).
3
Analyze the proof for sanity and puberty
The hadith 'The pen is lifted from three' removes accountability from the child and the insane, so no obligation.
This is a Sunnah ahad proof.
4
Analyze the proof for Islam
Quran 27:3 describes believers who establish prayer, implying that obligation applies only to Muslims.
The verse indicates that prayer (and thus wudu) is for those with faith.
5
Apply the distinction
Practice with examples: a child's wudu is valid; an insane person's wudu is not obligatory but valid; a disbeliever is not addressed.

Chapter on Wudu. The Hereafter. (69) And the conditions of its obligation are sanity, puberty, and Islam. Proof: (1) Abdullah ibn Umar entered upon Ibn Amir visiting him while he was ill, and he said: 'Won't you supplicate to Allah for me, O Ibn Umar?' He said: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say: No prayer is accepted without purification, and no charity from ill-gotten gains.' (Muslim, Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates that prayer is not valid without wudu. (2) And in the Hereafter, the reward is in this hadith: From Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'When a Muslim or believing servant performs wudu and washes his face, every sin he looked at with his eyes comes out with the water, or with the last drop of water...' (Tirmidhi) This hadith mentions the reward of wudu. Translation: (69) The condition for wudu being obligatory is that one be sane, adult, and Muslim. Explanation: Here eight conditions for wudu being obligatory are being mentioned. Among them are these three: that a person be [1] sane, [2] adult, and [3] Muslim. Then wudu becomes obligatory. If a person is not sane but insane, then neither prayer is obligatory upon him nor is wudu obligatory. However, if he does wudu and prays, his prayer will be valid, but it is not obligatory. Similarly, if he is not an adult (a child), then neither prayer is obligatory nor wudu. If a person is not Muslim (a disbeliever), then neither prayer nor wudu is obligatory. Each has its proof. Proof: (1) That one be sane and adult, its proof is this hadith: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah) This hadith indicates that there is no obligation on a child or an insane person, so wudu will not be obligatory. (2) There is an athar: 'Zakat is not obligatory on the wealth of a minor until prayer becomes obligatory upon him.' (Darqutni) This athar shows that a child has neither zakat on wealth nor wudu. (3) And being Muslim, its proof is this verse: 'Those who establish prayer and give zakat and of the Hereafter they are certain.' (Surah Naml 27:3) This verse indicates that one must have certainty in the Hereafter, i.e., be Muslim, then prayer is upon him and then wudu.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof lesson. It states three conditions for wudu to be obligatory: sanity, puberty, and Islam. The author explains that these are from eight conditions for the obligation of wudu. If any is missing, wudu is not obligatory. For sanity and puberty, the proof is the hadith of 'the pen is lifted' from the sleeper, child, and insane, meaning they are not held accountable. For Islam, the proof is Quran 27:3, which describes believers as those who establish prayer, indicating that only Muslims are addressed with the obligation. The commentary also clarifies that if an insane person or child performs wudu and prays, it is valid but not obligatory. Similarly, a disbeliever is not addressed with the obligation of wudu and prayer in this world.

Key Terms
وضو (wudu): Ritual ablution performed with water to remove ritual impurity (hadath).
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that necessitates wudu (minor hadath) or ghusl (major hadath).
مجنون (majnun): An insane person who lacks reason and is not legally responsible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence that wudu is not obligatory on a child?
A) Hadith of 'No prayer without purification'
B) Hadith of 'The pen is lifted from three'
C) Quran verse 'Those who establish prayer'
D) Athar from Ibn Abbas about zakat

Key Takeaway
Wudu is obligatory only upon the sane, adult Muslim; for the insane, child, and disbeliever, it is not required.

Condition for Obligation of Wudu: Ability to Use Sufficient Water
States the condition of ability to use sufficient water and its proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of ability to use sufficient water for the obligation of wudu and apply it to determine when tayammum replaces wudu.

Core Idea
Wudu is wajib only when water is sufficient and safe to use; otherwise tayammum becomes wajib.

Wudu is the key to prayer, but is it always obligatory? The Hanafi school teaches that the obligation of wudu hinges on a practical condition: you must have enough clean water and be able to use it without harm. This lesson unpacks that condition, known as 'qudrah ala istimal al-mai al-kafi', and proves it from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding this principle prevents hardship and aligns purification with divine mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wudu (or ghusl). The ruling is that it becomes wajib only when two sub-conditions are met: (a) sufficient water is present, and (b) the person is able to use it safely. If either fails, tayammum becomes wajib.
This is the fourth condition for wudu; earlier conditions include being Muslim, having reached puberty, and being sane.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 5:6, which commands tayammum when water is not found ('falam tajidu ma'an'). The same verse also mentions illness as a reason for tayammum, implying that harmful water is treated like absent water. Hadith from Abu Dharr confirms tayammum suffices even for ten years.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah in establishing the condition.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse commands tayammum explicitly when water is absent. By logical implication, when water is present and safe, the original command for wudu applies. The mention of illness shows that harm negates ability. Thus, ability (qudrah) is a necessary condition for wudu to be wajib.
The hadith extends the condition to long-term unavailability.
4
Note the consensus
This condition is muttafaq alayh across schools; there is no ikhtilaf on the principle. The differences that exist are about detailed applications, e.g., what constitutes 'sufficient' water.
Hanafi position: wudu is not wajib if water is insufficient or harmful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

( آیت ۴۳ سورۃ النساء۴) (۳) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ذر ... قال رسول الله ع الصعيد الطيب وضوء المسلم ولو الى عشر سنين (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الحب یتیم، ص ۵۳، نمبر ۳۳۲ / ترمذی شریف، باب ماجاء فی التیم للجب اذالم يسجد الماء ۳۲۰ نمبر نمبر۳۳۲ في ۱۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پانی نہ ملے تو دس سال تک جنسی تیم کر کے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ یعنی پانی نہ ملے یا پانی پر قدرت نہ ہو تو

Translation: (70) Ability to use sufficient water. Explanation: This is the fourth condition for wudu. If water sufficient for wudu is present, then wudu is obligatory; otherwise, tayammum is obligatory. Similarly, if one has the ability to use water, then it is obligatory; but if one is sick such that using water is harmful, then tayammum is obligatory. Therefore it is said that water should be sufficient and one should have the ability to use it. Proof: (1) In this verse: 'If you are in a state of major impurity, purify yourselves. But if you are ill or on a journey or one of you comes from the toilet or you have touched women and find no water, then seek clean earth and wipe your faces and hands with it...' (Surah Maidah 5:6). This verse indicates that if you cannot find water, perform tayammum. (2) Also in this verse (Surah Nisa 4:43). (3) Hadith: 'Clean earth is the wudu of a Muslim, even for ten years.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates that if water is not available, one can perform tayammum and pray for a long period.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof lesson on the fourth condition for the obligation of wudu: ability to use sufficient water. The author explains that if water is present and safe to use, wudu is obligatory; if not, tayammum becomes obligatory. The proofs are Quran 5:6 and 4:43, which command tayammum when water is absent or harmful. The hadith from Abu Dharr confirms that tayammum suffices even for ten years if water is unavailable. This condition ensures that the obligation of purification does not cause hardship.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
قدرة (qudrah): Ability to use water without harm or impediment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Wudu is obligatory anyway
B) Tayammum becomes obligatory
C) One may choose between wudu and tayammum
D) Prayer is not valid until health returns

Key Takeaway
Wudu is only wajib when you have both sufficient water and the ability to use it safely; otherwise, Allah has prescribed tayammum as a merciful substitute.

Condition for Wudu Obligation: Occurrence of Hadath
States the condition that hadath must have occurred for wudu to be obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that triggers the obligation of wudu and distinguish when wudu is wajib versus mustahabb.

Core Idea
Wudu is only obligatory when hadath occurs; renewal without hadath is recommended.

This passage explains the fifth condition for wudu: the actual occurrence of hadath (minor impurity). It clarifies that wudu is not required for every prayer if one remains in a state of purity. Rather, it becomes obligatory only after hadath. Renewing wudu without occurrence of hadath is considered mustahabb (recommended). The proof is a hadith from Anas ibn Malik showing the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being discussed (wudu) and its legal ruling (wajib/mustahabb) under different conditions.
Wudu is wajib when hadath occurs; it is mustahabb when no hadath.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the specific proof (hadith) cited and its source.
Hadith from Tirmidhi: Anas ibn Malik reported the Prophet and Companions prayed multiple prayers with one wudu.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling: the Companions' practice shows that renewal is not obligatory; wudu is only required after hadath.
The hadith explicitly states 'as long as we did not have hadath'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Acknowledge that the Shafi'i school differs, considering it mustahabb to renew wudu for each prayer.
This ikhtilaf does not affect the Hanafi mufta bihi position.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
State the operative ruling for fatwa: wudu is wajib upon hadath, and mustahabb to renew without hadath.
This is the standard Hanafi position with authority weight from later fatwa works.

Source Text

Translation: (71) And the occurrence of hadath (impurity). Explanation: This is the fifth condition for wudu. If minor hadath occurs, then wudu becomes obligatory. If no hadath has occurred, and one performs wudu, it is not obligatory, but performing wudu upon wudu is mustahabb (recommended). Proof: I heard Anas ibn Malik say: 'The Prophet would perform wudu for every prayer.' I asked: 'What did you use to do?' He said: 'We would pray all the prayers with one wudu as long as we did not have hadath.' (Tirmidhi)

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof lesson on the fifth condition: the actual occurrence of hadath. The author explains that wudu is only obligatory when minor hadath has taken place. If one is already in a state of wudu, it is not obligatory to renew it; however, doing so is recommended. The proof is the hadith of Anas, which shows that the Companions would maintain one wudu for multiple prayers until they had hadath. This establishes that wudu is only required after impurity occurs, not for each prayer.

Key Terms
حدث اصغر (hadath asghar): Minor ritual impurity that is removed by wudu (e.g., passing wind, urine, sleep).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; performing it earns reward, omitting it does not incur sin.

Key Takeaway
Wudu is only obligatory upon occurrence of hadath; renewing it without hadath is mustahabb.

Conditions for Wudu Becoming Obligatory
Explains when wudu is obligatory through two conditions with textual proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for wudu to become obligatory and identify when wudu is not required due to menstrual/postpartum bleeding or tight time.

Core Idea
Wudu is only obligatory when prayer is obligatory and time permits; hayd/nifas and extreme time pressure remove the obligation.

In this lesson we examine two crucial conditions that determine whether wudu becomes obligatory. The first relates to women in a state of menstruation or postpartum bleeding—since no prayer is required, wudu is not required. The second concerns a very tight prayer time where performing wudu would cause one to miss the prayer; in such a case, tayammum suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage and list the two conditions that must be absent for wudu to be obligatory: (1) absence of hayd and nifas, (2) non-tightness of time.
These are shurut al-wujub, not shurut al-sihha.
2
Examine the proof for hayd/nifas
Consider the hadith of Aisha where menstruating women are not required to make up prayers. This shows that when prayer is not obligatory, wudu is also not obligatory.
The same ruling applies to nifas due to similarity.
3
Examine the proof for tight time
Consider the athar of Ibn Abbas that permits tayammum when one fears missing the funeral prayer without wudu. This indicates that wudu is not obligatory when time is too tight.
The passage presents two interpretations: (a) for Eid/janaza, tayammum replaces wudu; (b) for regular prayers, tight time makes wudu immediately obligatory.
4
Understand the nuance of tight time
Distinguish between ample time (wudu can be delayed) and tight time (wudu becomes immediately obligatory to not miss the prayer). The exception is when the time is so tight that even performing wudu would cause missing the prayer—then tayammum is permitted, lifting the obligation of wudu.
This dual interpretation reflects different contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الوضوء
(۷۲) وعدم الحيض والنفاس (۷۳) وضيق الوقت .
ترجمه : (۷۲) حیض نہ ہو اور نفاس نہ ہو۔
تشریح : حیض نہ ہونا وضو کے لئے چھٹی شرط ہے، اور نفاس نہ ہونا ساتویں شرط ہے۔ اگر عورت کو حیض یا نفاس ہو تو اس پر نماز ہی واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے اس پر وضو بھی واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لئے فرمایا کہ حیض اور نفاس نہ ہوتب وضو واجب ہوگا ۔
وجه : ان امراة سألت عائشة أتقضى الحائض الصلاة فقالت أحرورية انت ؟ لقد كنا نحيض عند رسول الله الله فلا نقضى و لا نؤمر بالقضاء ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب فی الحائض لا تقضی الصلوۃ ،ص ۴۷، نمبر۲۶۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حائضہ نماز قضی نہیں کرے گی اس لئے اس پر وضو بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا، اور یہی حال نفاس والی عورت کا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۷۳) اور وقت تنگ نہ ہو۔
تشریح : اس عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وقت تنگ ہو تو عید اور نماز جنازہ کے لئے تیتم کر سکتا ہے اس کے لئے وضو واجب نہیں ۔ اور دوسرا مطلب شاید یہ ہے کہ وقت میں گنجائش ہو تو ابھی وضو کرنا واجب نہیں، بعد میں بھی وضو کر کے نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے ،لیکن وقت تنگ ہو تو ابھی نماز بھی پڑھنی ہے اس لئے ابھی وضو بھی واجب ہے۔
وجه : عن ابن عباس قال اذا خفت ان تفوتك الجنازة وانت على غير وضوء فتيمم و صلی. (مصنف ابن الى هيبة ٩٣ في الرجل ان يخاف ان تفوته الصلوة على الجنازة وهو غير متوضى ، ج ثانی، ص ۴۹۷ نمبر ۱۱۴۶۷، کتاب الجنائز ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز جنازہ فوت ہونے کا خوف ہو تو تیم کرسکتا ہے۔
Chapter on Wudu
(72) And the absence of menstruation and postpartum bleeding. (73) And tightness of time.
Translation (72): That there be no menstruation and no postpartum bleeding.
Explanation: The absence of menstruation is the sixth condition for wudu, and the absence of postpartum bleeding is the seventh condition. If a woman is menstruating or in postpartum bleeding, prayer is not obligatory upon her, therefore wudu is also not obligatory upon her. Hence it is said that when menstruation and postpartum bleeding are absent, wudu becomes obligatory.
Proof: A woman asked Aisha: 'Does the menstruating woman make up the prayer?' She said: 'Are you a Haruri? We used to menstruate in the presence of the Messenger of Allah, and we were not commanded to make them up.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on the menstruating woman not making up prayer, p. 47, no. 262) This hadith indicates that the menstruating woman will not make up the prayer, therefore wudu is not obligatory upon her, and the same applies to a woman with postpartum bleeding.
Translation (73): And that the time be not tight.
Explanation: The meaning of this phrase is that if the time is tight, one may perform tayammum for Eid and funeral prayer; wudu is not obligatory for that. The second meaning is perhaps that if there is ample time, wudu is not obligatory immediately; one can perform wudu later and pray. But if the time is tight, one must pray now, so wudu is also obligatory now.
Proof: Ibn Abbas said: 'If you fear that the funeral prayer will pass you by while you are without wudu, then perform tayammum and pray.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, p. 93, no. 11467, Book of Funerals) This athar shows that if there is fear of missing the funeral prayer, one may perform tayammum.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage explains two conditions for wudu to be obligatory. First, a woman must not be in a state of menstruation (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas), because in those states prayer is not required, and wudu is only required for prayer. The proof is the hadith of Aisha that menstruating women do not make up prayers. Second, the time for prayer must not be so tight that one would miss the prayer if one performed wudu; in that case, tayammum suffices, as shown by the narration from Ibn Abbas. Note the nuance: when time is ample, wudu is not immediately wajib; one may delay. But when time is tight, wudu becomes wajib immediately to enable prayer.

Key Terms
حیض (hayd): The monthly menstrual discharge from a woman's womb, which prevents prayer and fasting.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding after childbirth, similar to hayd in rulings.
ضیق الوقت (diiq al-waqt): Tightness of time: when the remaining time for a prayer is so short that performing wudu would cause one to miss the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition is wudu not obligatory for a woman?
A) When she is in the state of nifas
B) When she is traveling
C) When she is in the state of ritual purity
D) When she has performed ghusl

Key Takeaway
Wudu becomes obligatory only when prayer is obligatory and there is sufficient time to perform it.

Conditions for Valid Wudu: The Three Shurut
Lists the three conditions for wudu validity with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the validity of wudu in the Hanafi school and identify the dalil for each condition.

Core Idea
A wudu is valid only if water reaches all required skin, the water is pure, and no impurities or hadath are present on the body.

This lesson examines the three conditions (shurut) for a valid wudu according to the Hanafi school. These conditions are external to the act itself but must be satisfied for wudu to be legally effective. The source passage provides textual proofs from hadith, demonstrating how the Hanafi school derives these rulings from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
List the three conditions
Read the opening sentence: 'And its condition for correctness are three: the covering of the skin with water, the purification [of the water], and the cessation of what contradicts it from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and hadath.'
Memorize these three: umum al-basharah, tahur, and absence of impurities/hadath.
2
Analyze Condition 1: Umum al-basharah
Understand that water must reach every part of the skin that is required to be washed. The text gives examples: elbows, light beard. Proofs: Hadith of the heels (Muslim) and the man who left a nail spot (Muslim). The command 'aspighu al-wudu'' indicates obligation.
Any dry spot, even a hair's breadth, invalidates wudu.
3
Analyze Condition 2: Tahur
The water used must be pure and purifying (tahur). The passage does not provide a separate proof here, but this is a well-established condition from other sources.
Tahur water is water that is intrinsically pure and capable of purifying others.
4
Analyze Condition 3: Absence of contaminants
Break down the sub-conditions: no active hayd/nifas, no janabah, no madhi/urine/stool on the body, and no impurity above a dirham in size. The text gives hadith for each: Asma (hayd), Aisha (janabah), Ali (madhi), Safwan (minor hadath).
Impurities less than a dirham are excused; a dirham or more must be washed.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Consider a person who performs wudu but has a small spot of urine on their thigh (less than a dirham). According to the passage, this impurity is excused, so wudu is valid. If the spot is a dirham or more, wudu is invalid.
The dirham rule applies to thick impurities; for hadath like madhi, the presence itself invalidates wudu regardless of amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط صحته ثلاثة. عموم البشرة بالماء
الطهور (۷۵) وانقطاع ما ينافيه من حيض و نفاس وحدث
تشریح : یہ تین باتیں ہوں تب وضو صیح ہو گا [1] پہلی بات یہ ہے کہ جہاں جہاں پانی پہنچانا ہے کھال کی ان تمام حصوں پر پاک پانی پہنچادیا جائے ، بال برابر بھی کہیں سوکھا نہ رہے، مثلا کہنیوں پر پانی نہیں پہنچا، یا ہلکی ڈاڑھی میں کھال تک پانی نہیں پہنچا تو وضو نہیں ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمرو قال رجعنا مع رسول الله له من مكة الى المدينة حتى اذا كنا بماء بالطريق تعجل قوم عند العصر فتوضأ وا و هم عجال فانتهينا اليهم و اعقابهم تلوح لم يمسهـا الـمـاء فـقال رسول الله الا الله ويل للاعقاب من النار أسبغوا الوضوء . (مسلم شریف، باب وجوب غسل الرجلین بکمالها ص ۱۲۰، نمبر ۵۷۰/۲۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھال کا تھوڑا سا حصہ بھی سوکھا نہیں رہنا چاہئے ورنہ وضو نہیں ہو گا
(۲) اخبرني عمر بن الخطاب ان رجلا توضأ فترك موضع ظفر على قدمه فأبصر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : ارجع فأحسن وضوئک ، فرجع ثم صلی ۔ (مسلم شریف، باب وجوب استیعاب جميع اجزا مجمل الطهارة ص ۱۲۱، نمبر ۲۴۳ ۵۷۶) اس حدیث میں بھی کہ تھوڑی سی کھال بھی سوکھی نہیں رہنی چاہئے۔
لغت : البشرة: کھال کے اوپر کا حصہ عموم البشرة: تمام وہ کھال جس کا دھونا ضروری ہو۔
ترجمه : (۷۵) جو وضو کے منافی ہو وہ نہ ہو، مثلا حیض، نفاس ، اور حدث نہ ہوں ۔
تشریح : وضو درست ہونے کے لئے یہ دوسری شرط ہے کہ وضو کی جو منافی چیزیں ہیں، جسم پر وہ نہ ہوں تب وضو صحیح ہو گا مثلا حیض آرہا ہو، یا نفاس آرہا ہو تو اس زمانے میں وضو کرنے سے وضو نہیں ہوگا، یا عورت پاک ہو چکی ہے لیکن عورت پر حیض یا نفاس کا خون ایک درہم سے زیادہ لگا ہوا ہے تو اس وقت وضو کرنے سے اس وضو سے نماز درست نہیں ہوگی جب تک کہ اس کو دھو نہ لے۔ حدث کا دو مطلب ہے [1] حدث اکبر یعنی مرد یا عورت جنبی ہو تو اس وقت وضو درست نہیں ہے، جب تک کہ غسل نہ کر لے۔ [۲] اور دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وضو کے وقت تھوڑ اسا بھی پیشاب ظاہر ہو گیا، یا پیخانہ ظاہر ہو گیا، یامندی ظاہر ہوگئی تو اس وضو سے نماز جائز نہیں ہوگی، جب تک کہ دوبارہ وضو نہ کرے، یا وضو کرنے سے پہلے پیشاب یا پیخانہ یا مندی ظاہر ہوئی ، اور اس کی مقدار ایک درہم ہے تو اس حال میں وضو کرنے سے وضو نہیں ہوگا ، ہاں اس کو دھولے اور پھر سے وضو کرے تو جائز ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایک درہم سے کم نجاست غلیظہ معاف ہے، ایک درہم معاف نہیں ہے۔
وجه : (۱) حیض کا موقع نہ ہو، یا بدن پر حیض کا خون نہ ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ اسمـاء قـالـت جـانـت امرأة النبي فقالت أرأيت احدانا تحيض في الثوب كيف تصنع ؟ قال تحته ثم تقرصه بالماء و تنضحه و تصلى فيه بخاری، باب غسل الدم ص ۴۲ نمبر (۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حیض کا خون بدن پر نہ ہو۔ (۲) جنابت نہ ہو یا بدن پر منی نہ ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كنت اغسل الجنابة من ثوب النبى الله فيخرج الى الصلوة و ان بقع الماء فى ثوبه - بخاری شریف ، باب غسل المنى وفركه و نسل ما يصيب من المرأة ، ص ۴۲، نمبر ۲۲۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنابت بھی نہ کپڑے پر ہو اور نہ بدن پر ہو۔ (۳) ندی نہ ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عـن عـلـى قــال کـنـت رجلا مذاء فكنت استحيى ان اسأل النبى الله لمكان ابنته فأمرت المقداد بن الاسود فسأله فقال يغسل ذكره و يتوضا - ( مسلم شریف ، باب المذی ،ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۶۹۵/۳۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مدی بدن پر ہو تو اس کو دھولے ورنہ وضو نہیں ہوگا۔ (۴) حدث اصغر نہ ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن صفوان بن عسال قال كان رسول الله الله يأمرنا اذا كنا سفرا ان لا ننزع خفافنا ثلاثة ايام و ليليهن الا من جنابة و لكن من غائط و بول و نوم ۔ (ترمذی شریف،
And its condition for correctness are three: (1) The covering of the skin with water. (2) The purification [of the water]. (75) And the cessation of what contradicts it from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and hadath.
Explanation: When these three things are present, wudu will be correct. The first is that wherever water must be reached, pure water must reach all those parts of the skin; not even a hair's breadth should remain dry. For example, if water does not reach the elbows, or in a light beard water does not reach the skin, then wudu is not valid.
Proof: (1) In this hadith: 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr said: We returned with the Messenger of Allah from Mecca to Medina until when we were at a water source on the road, some people hastened at 'Asr and performed wudu hurriedly. We reached them and their heels were dry, water had not touched them. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Woe to the heels from the Fire! Perform wudu thoroughly.' (Muslim, chapter on obligation of washing both feet completely, p. 120, no. 570/241) This hadith indicates that even a small part of the skin must not remain dry; otherwise wudu is not valid. (2) 'Umar ibn al-Khattab informed me that a man performed wudu and left the place of a nail on his foot. The Prophet saw him and said: 'Go back and improve your wudu.' So he went back and then prayed. (Muslim, chapter on obligation of covering all parts of purification, p. 121, no. 243/576) This hadith also indicates that even a small bit of skin should not remain dry.
Lexicon: al-basharah: the upper part of the skin. 'umum al-basharah: all the skin that is necessary to wash.
Translation (75): That which contradicts wudu be absent, such as menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and hadath.
Explanation: This is the second condition for the correctness of wudu: that the things which contradict wudu not be present on the body. For example, if menstruation is ongoing, or postpartum bleeding is ongoing, then performing wudu during that time will not result in a valid wudu. Or if a woman has become pure but has menstrual or postpartum blood on her body more than a dirham, then performing wudu at that time will not make the prayer valid until she washes it off. Hadath has two meanings: (1) Major hadath – a man or woman in a state of janabah; then wudu is not valid until ghusl is performed. (2) The second meaning is that if during wudu a little urine, stool, or madhi appears, then that wudu does not make prayer permissible until wudu is renewed. Or if before wudu, urine, stool, or madhi appeared and its amount is a dirham, then wudu performed in that state is not valid. Yes, if one washes it and then performs wudu again, it becomes permissible. Because less than a dirham of thick impurity is forgiven; a dirham is not forgiven.
Proofs: (1) For the absence of menstrual blood on the body: Asma said: A woman came to the Prophet and said: 'What do you think if one of us menstruates in her garment, what should she do?' He said: 'Scrape it, then rub it with water, sprinkle with water, and pray in it.' (Bukhari, chapter on washing blood, p. 42 no. 22) This hadith indicates that menstrual blood should not be on the body. (2) For the absence of janabah or semen on the body: Aisha said: I used to wash janabah from the Prophet's garment, and he would go out to prayer while water spots were still on his garment. (Bukhari, chapter on washing semen and rubbing it, p. 42 no. 229) This hadith indicates that janabah should not be on the garment or body. (3) For the absence of madhi: 'Ali said: I was a man who discharged madhi frequently, and I felt shy to ask the Prophet because of his daughter. So I asked Miqdad ibn al-Aswad to ask him, and he said: 'He should wash his penis and perform wudu.' (Muslim, chapter on madhi, p. 138 no. 695/303) This hadith indicates that if madhi is on the body, one must wash it; otherwise wudu is not valid. (4) For the absence of minor hadath: Safwan ibn 'Assal said: The Messenger of Allah used to command us, when we were traveling, not to remove our khuffs for three days and nights except due to janabah, but due to stool, urine, and sleep. (Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage enumerates the three conditions (shurut) for a valid wudu according to the Hanafi school. First, water must reach all the required skin areas (umum al-basharah). The proofs are the hadiths warning against leaving any part dry, like the heels, and the command to 'improve your wudu' when a spot was missed. Second, the water used must be pure (tahur). Third, nothing that contradicts wudu must be present on the body: that includes active hayd/nifas blood flow, or residual blood above a dirham, janabah (major impurity), madhi, or any minor hadath (like urine, stool, wind, sleep). The commentary explains that if any of these exist, wudu is either invalid or the prayer performed with that wudu will not be valid until the impurity is removed. The proofs for the third condition come from various hadith: the hadith of Asma for menstrual blood, Aisha for janabah, 'Ali for madhi, and Safwan for minor hadath. Note that for impurities less than a dirham in size, they are excused; a dirham or more must be washed.

Key Terms
البشرة (al-basharah): The visible skin surface that must be washed during wudu or ghusl.
عموم البشرة ('umum al-basharah): The requirement that water must reach every part of the skin that is obligated to be washed.
الطهور (al-tahur): Ritually pure water that has not been used and is from a pure source.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu; includes major (janabah) and minor (e.g., urine, wind).
مذی (madhi): A clear, sticky fluid that exits due to arousal; it nullifies wudu but does not require ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person performs wudu while there is a drop of urine (size of a dirham) on their thigh?
A) Wudu is valid because the impurity is small.
B) Wudu is valid but must be repeated to be safe.
C) Wudu is invalid because an impurity of a dirham or more prevents validity.
D) Wudu is valid but the prayer is not accepted.

Key Takeaway
The three conditions for valid wudu are essential: water coverage, water purity, and absence of ritual impurity/contamination; neglecting any condition invalidates wudu.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Conditions for Valid Wudu: Absence of Menstruation, Postpartum Bleeding, and Hadath
Ruling with hadith proofs on conditions for wudu validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid wudu and apply the Hanafi ruling on the one-dirham threshold for heavy impurity.

Core Idea
Wudu is invalid if hadath, hayd, nifas, or heavy impurity (≥1 dirham) is present.

Wudu is a prerequisite for prayer, but it is not always valid. This lesson explores the second condition for wudu: the body must be free from impurities that contradict it. We will examine the categories of hadath, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding, as well as the fiqhi nuance of the one-dirham threshold for heavy filth, supported by hadith proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The text states that wudu requires 'tahur' (purity from filth) and cessation of what contradicts it. Identify what these contradictory elements are.
The condition is: no hayd, nifas, or hadath on the body.
2
Understand the categories of impurities
Hadath is divided into major (janabah) and minor (urine, feces, madhi, wind, sleep). Hayd and nifas are considered major hadath. Distinguish each.
3
Note the dirham threshold
The text introduces a one-dirham threshold for heavy impurity (najisah ghalizah). Impurity less than a dirham is excused; one dirham or more must be washed.
This threshold applies to blood of hayd/nifas and other filth.
4
Review the hadith proofs
The author cites four hadith: one for hayd (Asma), one for janabah (Aisha), one for madhi (Ali), and one for minor hadath (Safwan). Understand how each supports the condition.
5
Apply to hypotheticals
Consider scenarios: a woman with menstrual blood less than a dirham, a man with madhi discharge, a traveler with minor hadath. Determine wudu validity based on the ruling.

Purity and cessation of what contradicts it, such as menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and hadath. (2) Umar ibn al-Khattab informed me that a man performed wudu and left a spot of a nail on his foot; the Prophet saw him and said: 'Go back and make your wudu well.' So he returned and then prayed. (Muslim, chapter on obligation of encompassing all parts of the summary of purification, p. 121, no. 243/576) This hadith also indicates that not even a little skin should remain dry. Lexicon: al-basharah: the upper part of the skin; 'umum al-basharah: all the skin that must be washed. Translation: (75) That which contradicts wudu should not exist, such as menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and hadath. Explanation: For wudu to be valid, this is the second condition: that things contradicting wudu are not present on the body. Then wudu will be valid. For example, if menstruation is occurring, or postpartum bleeding is occurring, then at that time performing wudu will not make wudu. Or if a woman has become pure, but the blood of menstruation or postpartum bleeding more than one dirham is on her body, then at that time performing wudu will not make the prayer valid until she washes it off. Hadath has two meanings: [1] Major hadath (janabah) – if a man or woman is in a state of janabah, then wudu is not valid at that time until they perform ghusl. [2] The second meaning is that if during wudu a little urine appears, or feces appears, or madhi appears, then prayer with that wudu is not permissible until wudu is repeated. Or if before wudu, urine, feces, or madhi appeared, and its amount is one dirham, then performing wudu in that state will not make wudu valid. However, if they wash it and then perform wudu again, it will be permissible. Because less than one dirham of heavy impurity is excused; one dirham is not excused. Evidence: (1) That the time of menstruation not be present, or blood of menstruation not be on the body – the proof for this is the hadith: Asma said: A woman came to the Prophet and said: 'What do you think if one of us menstruates in her garment – how should she act?' He said: 'She should scrape it, then rub it with water, then sprinkle it, and pray in it.' (Bukhari, chapter on washing blood, p. 42, no. 22) This hadith indicates that menstrual blood should not be on the body. (2) That janabah not be present, or semen not be on the body – the proof for this is the hadith: From Aisha, she said: I used to wash janabah from the garment of the Prophet, then he would go out to prayer while traces of water were on his garment. (Bukhari, chapter on washing semen and rubbing and brushing what touches from the woman, p. 42, no. 229) This hadith indicates that janabah should not be on the garment or on the body. (3) That madhi not be present – the proof for this is the hadith: From Ali, he said: I was a man who secreted madhi, and I was shy to ask the Prophet because of his daughter, so I asked Miqdad ibn al-Aswad to ask him, and he said: 'He should wash his private part and perform wudu.' (Muslim, chapter on madhi, p. 138, no. 695/303) This hadith indicates that if madhi is on the body, he should wash it; otherwise wudu is not valid. (4) That minor hadath not be present – the proof for this is the hadith: From Safwan ibn Assal, he said: The Messenger of Allah used to command us, when we were traveling, not to remove our leather socks for three days and nights except from janabah, but from feces, urine, and sleep. (Tirmidhi,
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding conditions for the validity of wudu. The matn states that wudu requires taharah (purity from filth) and cessation of things that contradict it: menstruation (hayd), postpartum bleeding (nifas), and hadath (impurity). The author explains that these must be absent from the body. He then provides a linguistic note on 'basharah' (skin). The Urdu translation and commentary elaborate: condition two for wudu is that no contradictory matters exist on the body. If a woman is menstruating or in postpartum bleeding, her wudu is invalid. Even if she is pure but has blood stains exceeding one dirham, wudu is incomplete until she washes it. Hadath is divided into major (janabah, requiring ghusl) and minor (urine, feces, madhi, sleep, wind). If minor hadath occurs during wudu, the wudu is invalidated; if it occurred before wudu, one must wash the impurity (if it is a physical impurity) and then perform wudu anew. The amount of heavy impurity (najisah ghalizah) equal to one dirham or more prevents validity; less is excused. The author then provides proofs from hadith for each category: the hadith of Asma about menstrual blood, of Aisha about janabah, of Ali about madhi, and of Safwan about minor hadath from bodily exits and sleep. These hadith establish the necessity of being free from these impurities for wudu to be valid. The ruling is standard in the Hanafi school: the presence of these nullifiers makes wudu invalid.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): In this passage, hadath refers to both major (janabah) and minor (urine, feces, madhi, wind, sleep) impurities that invalidate wudu.
الطهور (al-tahur): Purity from physical filth (najis) such as urine, blood, etc. In this context, it is a condition for wudu: the body must be clean of anything that invalidates wudu.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding after childbirth. It is considered a major hadath that prevents wudu and requires ghusl after cessation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on wudu if a woman has menstrual blood on her body less than one dirham?
A) Wudu is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Wudu is valid because the blood is less than a dirham and thus excused.
C) Wudu is valid only if she washes the blood off first.
D) Wudu is invalid because any amount of menstrual blood nullifies wudu.

Key Takeaway
Wudu is valid only when the body is free from hayd, nifas, and all forms of hadath, with a one-dirham threshold for heavy impurity.

Removal of Barriers in Wudu: The Condition of Water Reaching the Skin
Ruling with proof about removing barriers in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that barriers preventing water from reaching the skin invalidate wudu, and identify which substances constitute such barriers.

Core Idea
A waterproof barrier on the skin during wudu blocks the obligation of washing, thus invalidating the worship.

This passage addresses a critical condition for the validity of wudu: water must come into direct contact with each required part of the skin. The text gives examples like wax and fat and provides evidence from the practice of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) regarding dye. We will explore the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage states it is a condition (shart) for wudu that no barrier prevents water from reaching the skin. If such a barrier exists, that part remains unwashed, making wudu invalid.
The text says 'zawal ma yamna' wusul al-ma' ila al-jasad' – removal of what prevents water reaching the body.
2
Analyse the Proof
The author cites two proofs: the general obligation to wash the skin (from an earlier hadith) and a specific athar from Aisha. In the athar, Aisha commands a woman to remove her khidab (dye) because it blocks water. This directly supports the ruling.
The hadith is mursal (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in practice by the Hanafi school.
3
Apply to Contemporary Examples
Analogous substances include nail polish, waterproof makeup, glue, paint, and any coating that forms a waterproof layer. Non-waterproof oils or perfumes that do not block water are excused.
The key is whether water can penetrate the substance to reach the skin.

Explanation: On the body parts of wudu, if there is a thing that does not allow water to reach the skin, such as wax or fat, these things do not allow water to reach the skin, so they should not be present, then wudu will be valid. Evidence: (1) The hadith passed earlier that reaching water to the skin is necessary, and these things do not allow water to reach the skin, so these things should not be present. Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that for wudu to be valid, no barrier may exist on the skin that prevents water from reaching it. The matn mentions examples such as wax (sham') and fat (shahm). The Urdu commentary explains that if such substances are present on the limbs of wudu, they prevent water from contacting the skin, thereby invalidating wudu. The evidence (wajh) is twofold: first, the general hadith (from earlier) that water must reach the entire skin; second, a specific athar (narration) from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) regarding a woman who had dye (khidab) on her hand while performing wudu. Aisha instructed her to remove it so that water could reach the skin. This establishes that any substance that blocks water must be removed before or during wudu. The ruling applies to any waterproof substance, such as paint, nail polish, glue, etc. The Hanafi school considers this a condition for the validity of wudu; if water cannot reach any part of the limb due to such a barrier, that limb remains unwashed, and wudu is incomplete.

Key Terms
خضاب (khidab): A dye or stain applied to the skin, typically henna. Used here as an example of a barrier that must be removed for wudu.
شمع (sham‘): Wax. Used as an example of a waterproof barrier that must be removed before wudu.
شحم (shahm): Fat or grease. Used as an example of a waterproof barrier that must be removed before wudu.

Ruling on Washing the Beard in Wudu
Ruling on beard washing in wudu with three categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings for thick beard, thin beard, and hair below the face in wudu, and apply the Hanafi mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Washing the outer part of a thick beard is wajib; the skin underneath is excused due to hardship.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text clarifies the ruling on washing the beard during wudu. The beard is categorized into three types based on density and location, each with a distinct obligation. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct wudu and avoiding common errors. The passage also provides the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, which takes into account the principle of ease (taysir) for thick beards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three beard categories
The passage divides the beard into: (1) thin beard where skin is visible, (2) thick beard within the face boundary, and (3) hair hanging below the face boundary.
Density (thin vs thick) and location (within or below face) are the two criteria.
2
State the ruling for each category
For thin beard: wajib to wet the skin. For thick beard: wajib to wash the outer part only. For hair below face: not wajib, but mustahabb.
This reflects the Hanafi position of ease for thick beards.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The hadith of Umar (cut off in text) requires water to reach every part of the skin. However, due to hardship (mashaqqa) for thick beards, the obligation is limited to the outer surface.
Waiving the obligation for the skin under thick beard is an example of istihsan based on difficulty.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school requires washing the skin under a thick beard. The Hanafi school eases this due to hardship, making the outer part sufficient.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both are valid.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
A man with a thick, bushy beard that completely hides the chin must ensure water covers the outer surface of the beard, but does not need to penetrate to the skin. For a thin, sparse beard, he must wet the skin.
The ruling applies to all wudu, not just initial washing; keeping the beard dry underneath does not invalidate wudu.

فصل: في تمام احكام الوضوء )

(77) It is obligatory to wash the outer part of a thick beard, according to the most correct view that is given for fatwa. And it is obligatory to make water reach the skin of the beard. Chapter: On the complete rulings of wudu. Translation: (77) Washing the outer part of a thick beard is obligatory, this is the relied-upon opinion. And for a thin beard, it is obligatory to make water reach the skin. And it is not obligatory to make water reach the hair that hangs below the circle of the face. Explanation: From here, three cases of the beard are being explained, and each has a separate ruling. [1] Where the beard is thin so that the skin of the face is visible, there it is obligatory to make water reach the skin. [2] Where the beard is thick and it is within the circle of the face, there it is not obligatory to make water reach the inside; merely washing the outer beard is sufficient. [3] And the beard that hangs below the circle of the face, whether it is thin or thick beard, it is not obligatory to make water reach its inside; however, it is recommended. Evidence: (1) In the hadith that came earlier, it is stated that making water reach the skin is necessary. Therefore, where the beard is thin and the skin of the face is visible, it is obligatory to make water reach. The hadith is: Umar ibn al-Khattab informed me that a man performed wudu and left a spot of a nail on his foot...
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on the beard during wudu. The matn states two obligations: washing the visible outer part of a thick beard (al-lihyah al-kaththah) is wajib, and making water reach the skin underneath the beard is also wajib. However, the Urdu commentary clarifies the details: The beard is categorized into three types based on density and location. First, if the beard is thin so that the skin is visible, then it is wajib to wash both the hair and the skin underneath. Second, if the beard is thick (dense) and it grows within the natural boundary of the face (the area that is considered part of the face for wudu), then only the outer surface of the beard must be washed; it is not wajib to wet the inner skin because it is hidden. Third, any hair that hangs below the chin (outside the face boundary) is not wajib to wash at all, but it is recommended (mustahabb). The evidence (wajh) is the hadith of Umar mentioned earlier, which requires water to reach every bit of skin. For thick beard, the ruling is eased due to hardship. The relied-upon position (asahh ma yuffa bihi) is that washing the outer part of a thick beard is sufficient, and water does not need to reach the skin. This is a Hanafi-specific ruling; the Shafi'i school, for example, requires washing the skin even under a thick beard. The passage also notes that for a thin beard, the skin must be wetted, which aligns with the general rule.

Key Terms
اللحية الكتة (al-lihyah al-kaththah): A thick, dense beard where the skin is not visible through the hair.
اللحية الخفيفة (al-lihyah al-khafifah): A thin beard where the skin is visible.
ما تحت الذقن (ma tahta al-dhaqan): Hair hanging below the chin, outside the face boundary for wudu.

D) It is not required to be touched at all.

Key Takeaway
For a thick beard within the face boundary, washing the outer hair is wajib; the skin underneath is excused due to hardship.

Removing Barriers to Water in Wudu
Ruling on necessity of removing substances that block water from skin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on barriers that prevent water from reaching the skin in wudu and explain the proof from the athar of Aisha.

Core Idea
Any substance that blocks water from reaching the skin must be removed for wudu to be valid.

In wudu, it is fard to wash the specified limbs. But what if there is a substance on the skin that prevents water from contacting it? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that such barriers must be removed, supported by a clear proof from the Sunnah. The passage from Thamaratun Najah presents the ruling and provides evidence from the practice of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening statement: 'And removal of what prevents water from reaching the body, like wax and fat.' Note that the author states the necessity of removal.
The ruling is that removal is wajib.
2
Locate the Proof
Find the two proofs cited: (1) a prior hadith establishing the obligation of water reaching the skin, and (2) the specific athar from Aisha regarding henna.
The athar is explicit in commanding removal.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The command 'اسلتيه' (remove it) directly indicates that any substance blocking water must be removed. The explanation by Abu Ubaydah reinforces that it must be rubbed off and discarded.
This establishes the general principle for all barriers.
4
Apply to Examples
Consider the given examples: wax, fat, henna. Determine if each forms a barrier. If yes, removal is required.
The key is whether water can reach the skin.

Translation: (76) Whatever prevents water from reaching the body should not be present, like wax and fat. Explanation: On the body for ablution, if there is something that prevents water from reaching the skin, like wax or fat, these things prevent water from reaching the skin, so they should not be present, then the ablution will be valid. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding obstacles that prevent water from reaching the skin during wudu. The author begins by stating the ruling: removal of such obstacles is necessary. Examples given are wax and fat, which form a barrier. The commentary explains that if such substances exist on the limbs to be washed, wudu is not valid until they are removed. The proof is drawn from two sources: first, a prior hadith (not quoted in full) establishing that water must reach the skin; second, an athar from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who instructed a woman with henna to remove it before wudu. Henna, if it forms a layer, prevents water from reaching the skin, so it must be removed. Abu Ubaydah explains that 'remove it' means to rub it off and discard it. This shows that any barrier, whether wax, fat, or henna, must be eliminated for wudu to be valid.

Key Terms
ما يمنع وصول الماء (ma yamna' wusul al-ma'): Any substance, solid or thick, that blocks water from contacting the skin during wudu or ghusl.
الخضاب (al-khidab): A dye or paste (like henna) applied to the skin or hair, which may create a barrier if it forms a coating.

Rulings on Washing the Beard in Wudu
Explains three beard cases with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings for washing the beard in wudu, distinguish between wajib and mustahabb, and cite the key proofs.

Core Idea
A thick beard only needs surface washing; a thin beard requires water to reach the skin; hanging beard interior is mustahabb, not wajib.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah clarifies a common point of confusion in wudu: to what extent must water reach the beard? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced classification based on beard density and location, supported by hadith and athar. Let's work through the three cases and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses three distinct beard states in wudu: thin beard (skin visible), thick beard within the face circle, and beard hanging below the face circle. For each, the ruling is either wajib or mustahabb.
The face circle (da'irat al-wajh) is from the forehead hairline to the chin.
2
Locate the dalil
Each ruling is supported by specific evidence: the hadith of the man with a dry spot (thin beard), the practice of Ali (thick beard surface), and the Prophet's combing of the hanging beard (mustahabb).
The proofs include hadith, sahabi/ tabi'i statements, and actions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the thin beard, the hadith commands thorough washing; for the thick beard, water flowing over is sufficient; for the hanging beard, the Prophet's occasional combing shows desirability, not obligation.
The difference in evidence quality explains the difference in ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is intra-Hanafi difference: some earlier Hanafis considered inner thick beard washing wajib. Cross-madhhab: Shafi'is oblige washing all beard hair.
The text endorses the view that only outer surface is wajib for thick beards.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The phrase 'fi asahh ma yufa bihi' indicates this is the relied-upon position. It is supported by multiple proofs and the practice of early Muslims.
This is the mufta bihi for Hanafis today.

فصل : في تمام احكام الوضوء (۷۷) يجب غسل ظاهر اللحية الكثة في اصح ما يفتى به . ويجب ايصال الماء الى بشرة اللحية الخفيفة. ولا يجب ايصال الماء الى المسترسل من الشعر عن دائرة الوجه. ترجمه : (۷۷) گھنی ڈاڑھی کے ظاہری حصے کو دھونا واجب ہے بھیجے مفتی بہ قول یہی ہے، اور ملکی ڈاڑھی کی کھال تک پانی پہنچانا واجب ہے۔ اور چہرے کے دائرے سے لٹکے ہوئے بال تک پانی پہچانا واجب نہیں ہے۔ تشریح : یہاں سے ڈاڑھی کی تین صورتیں بیان کی جارہی ہیں، اور ہر ایک کا حکم الگ الگ ہے۔ [1] ڈاڑھی جہاں ہلکی ہو کہ چہرے کی کھال نظر آتی ہو وہاں کھال تک پانی پہنچانا واجب ہے [۲] ڈاڑھی جہاں گھنی ہو اور وہ چہرے کے دائرے کے ساتھ ہو تو وہاں اندر پانی پہچانا واجب نہیں ہے ،صرف ظاہری ڈاڑھی کو دھودینا کافی ہے [۳] اور جو ڈاڑھی چہرے کے دائرے سے نیچے لٹکی ہوئی ہو چاہے وہ ملکی ڈاڑھی ہو ی گھنی داڑھی ہو اس کے اندر پانی پہنچانا واجب نہیں ہے، البتہ مستحب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) او پر حدیث میں آیا کہ کھال تک پانی پہنچا نا ضروری ہے، اس لئے جہاں ڈاڑھی ہلکی ہے اور چہرے کی کھال نظر آ رہی ہے وہاں پانی پہچانا واجب ہوگا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ اخبرنی عمر بن الخطاب ان رجلا توضأ فترک موضع ظفر علی الخفيفة. فأبصر النبى الله الله فقال : ارجع فأحسن وضوئک ، فرجع ثم صلی . (مسلم شریف ، باب وجوب استیعاب جميع اجزا محل الطهارة ،ص ۱۲۱، نمبر ۵۷۶/۲۴۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تھوڑی سی کھال بھی سوکھی نہیں رہنی چاہئے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث کے اشارے سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ گھنی ڈاڑھی کے اوپر پانی پہنچ جانا کافی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال دخل علی علی یعنی ابی طالب و قد اهرق الماء ..... ثم أخذ بكفه اليمنى قبضة من ماء فصبها على ناصيته فتركها تستن على وجهه ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب صفة وضوء النبی ، ص ۲۷، نمبر ۱۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پیشانی کے شروع سے تھوڑی کے نیچے تک پانی بہایا ، جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ ڈاڑھی کے اوپر پانی بہنا کافی ہے۔ (۳) اس قول تابعی میں اس کی صراحت ہے کہ گھنی ڈاڑھی پر پانی بہہ جانا کافی ہے۔ عن ابی عالیة قال حسبک ما سأل من وجهک علی لحیتک ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، باب من كان لا تخلل لحية و یقول یکفیک ما سال علیها ، ج اول ص ۲۱، نمبر ۱۲۰) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ ڈاڑھی پر جو پانی گرے وہی کافی ہے۔ (۴) اور لٹکی ہوئی ڈاڑھی میں خلال کرنا مستحب ہے، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ۔عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله الا الله كان اذا توضأ أخذ كفا من ماء فأدخله تحت حنكه فخلل به لحيته ، و قال هكذا امرني ربی عز و جل ۔ (ابوداود شریف ، باب تخلیل اللحیة، ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۱۴۵ ترمذی شریف، باب تخلیل اللحیة، ص ۱۴ نمبر ۳۱ رابن ماجه شریف، باب ماجاء فی تقلیل اللحية، ص ۶۳ نمبر ۴۲۹) (۵) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ لٹکی ہوئی ڈاڑھی میں خلال فرمایا کرتے تھے عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله لا اذا توضأعرک عارضیه بعض العرك ثم شبك لحيته بأصابعه من تحتها - (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ما جاء تخلیل اللحیتہ ص ۶۳ نمبر ۴۲۳۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ڈاڑھی کے نیچے سے خلال کرتے تھے ۔ (4) اس عمل صحابی سے استحباب کا پتہ چلتا ہے۔ ان ابن عمر كان اذا توضأ يعرک عارضیه و يشبك لحيته باصابعه احيانا و یترک احیانا (سنن بیہقی ، باب عرک العارضین ، ج اول ،ص ۹۲ نمبر (۲۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کبھی ڈاڑھی میں خلال کرتے تھے اور کبھی چھوڑ دیتے تھے، جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ گھنی ڈاڑھی ہو تو اندر پانی پہچانا فرض نہیں ہے۔ (۷) عبد الرحمن بن ابى ليلى قال : ان استطعت ان تبلغ بالماء اصول اللحية فافعل . (مصنف ابن ابی هیة ، افی غسل اللحية في الوضوء، ج اول ص ۲۲ نمبر ۱۲۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ڈاڑھی ہلکی ہو اور بال کی جڑ تک پانی پہونچا سکتے ہو تو وہاں تک پانی پہونچاو۔ لغت : الکثیہ گھنی ڈاڑھی ۔ الخفيفة : ہلکی ۔المستر سل : رسل سے مشتق ہے لٹکا ہوا ہونا۔ دائرۃ الوجہ : چہرے کا دائرہ ،تھوڑی تک کے حصے کو چہرے کا دائرہ کہتے ہیں۔
Section on completing the rulings of ablution. (77) It is obligatory to wash the outer part of the thick beard in the most correct view for fatwa. And it is obligatory to make water reach the skin of the thin beard. And it is not obligatory to make water reach the hanging hair (that hangs down) from the circle of the face. Translation: (77) Washing the outer part of a thick beard is wajib, and this is the preferred opinion for fatwa; and making water reach the skin of a thin beard is wajib; and making water reach hair hanging below the circle of the face is not wajib. Explanation: From here, three cases of the beard are explained, each with a different ruling. [1] Where the beard is thin such that the skin of the face is visible, it is wajib to make water reach the skin. [2] Where the beard is thick and it is within the circle of the face, it is not wajib to make water reach the inside; only washing the outer part of the beard is sufficient. [3] As for beard that hangs below the circle of the face, whether it is thin or thick, it is not wajib to make water reach the inside; rather it is mustahabb. Proofs: (1) The hadith mentioned earlier that it is necessary for water to reach the skin, so where the beard is thin and the skin is visible, making water reach is wajib. The hadith is: Umar ibn al-Khattab informed me that a man performed ablution and left a spot the size of a fingernail dry. The Prophet saw him and said: 'Go back and perform ablution properly.' So he returned and then prayed. (Muslim, chapter on necessity of covering all parts of the place of purification, p.121, no.576/243) This hadith indicates that even a small area of skin must not remain dry. (2) This hadith indicates that for a thick beard, water flowing over the surface is sufficient. From Ibn Abbas: 'Ali ibn Abi Talib entered while he had poured water... then he took a handful of water in his right hand and poured it over his forehead and let it flow over his face.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on description of the Prophet's ablution, p.27, no.117) This shows that water flowing over the beard is sufficient. (3) This statement of a Tabi'i explicitly states that water flowing over the thick beard is sufficient. From Abu Aliyah: 'It is sufficient for you what flows from your face onto your beard.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who did not comb the beard and said what flows over it is sufficient, vol.1, p.21, no.120) (4) Combing the hanging beard is mustahabb, and for this is the hadith: From Anas ibn Malik: 'When the Messenger of Allah performed ablution, he took a handful of water, put it under his chin, and combed his beard with it, and said: 'My Lord, the Mighty and Majestic, commanded me to do this.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on combing the beard, p.131, no.145; Tirmidhi, chapter on combing the beard, p.14, no.31; Ibn Majah, chapter on what is reported about combing the beard, p.63, no.429) (5) In this hadith also: he used to comb the hanging beard. From Ibn Umar: 'When the Messenger of Allah performed ablution, he would rub his cheeks a little and then interlace his beard with his fingers from below.' (Ibn Majah, chapter on what is reported about combing the beard, p.63, no.4232) (6) From the action of a Sahabi, desirability is understood. Ibn Umar used to sometimes comb his beard and sometimes leave it. (Sunan Bayhaqi, chapter on rubbing the cheeks, vol.1, p.92, no.25) This indicates that for a thick beard, making water reach inside is not fard. (7) Abdur Rahman ibn Abi Layla said: 'If you can make water reach the roots of the beard, do so.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, regarding washing the beard in ablution, vol.1, p.22, no.127) This indicates that for a thin beard, one should make water reach the roots. Lexicon: al-kaththah = thick beard; al-khafifah = thin; al-mustarsil = derived from rasala, hanging; da'irat al-wajh = the circle of the face, the area up to the chin is called the circle of the face.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with multiple proofs concerning the obligation of washing the beard during wudu. The author provides a detailed classification covering three scenarios. First, for a thin beard where the skin is visible, it is wajib to make water reach the skin itself, as water must touch every part of the face. The hadith of the man who left a fingernail-sized spot dry proves this: the Prophet commanded him to repeat his wudu, emphasizing that no area, even under a thin beard, may remain dry. Second, for a thick beard that grows within the circle of the face (i.e., the area from the forehead to the chin), it is sufficient to wash only the outer surface of the beard; water does not need to reach the skin underneath. Evidence includes the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib, who poured water on his forehead and let it flow over his face, indicating that water simply flowing over the beard suffices. The statement of Abu Aliyah confirms this: water that flows over the face and onto the beard is adequate. Third, for the beard that hangs below the circle of the face (i.e., on the neck), it is not wajib to wash the inner part; rather, it is mustahabb. The Prophet's action of combing his beard with water under the chin, and similarly Ibn Umar's practice of sometimes combing and sometimes not, demonstrate that this is a recommended act, not an obligation. The hadith of Anas explicitly states that the Prophet was commanded to do so, but the command is interpreted as istihbab (desirability) rather than wujub because it is not always done. Finally, for a thin beard, the instruction of Abdur Rahman ibn Abi Layla to reach the roots applies. In summary, the ruling hinges on the density and location of the beard: thin within the circle requires washing the skin; thick within the circle requires only surface washing; hanging beard requires no internal washing, but it is meritorious.

Key Terms
اللحية الكثة (al-lihyah al-kaththah): A thick beard where the skin underneath is not visible through the hair.
دائرة الوجه (da'irat al-wajh): The boundary of the face: from the forehead hairline to the chin, including the cheeks and beard area within this perimeter.
المسترسل (al-mustarsil): The part of the beard that hangs down below the circle of the face, typically on the neck.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT an evidence cited for the ruling on the thick beard within the face circle?
A) Hadith of Ali pouring water on his forehead.
B) Statement of Abu Aliyah.
C) Hadith of the man with a dry fingernail spot.
D) Action of Ibn Umar combing his beard.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of washing the beard in wudu depends on its density and location: thin beards require skin contact, thick beards only surface washing, and hanging beards have no inner obligation.

Ruling on Washing Inner Lips in Wudu
States that the inner part of the lips when closed is not wajib to wash

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for washing the inner lips in wudu and explain why it is not wajib according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The inner lips are not wajib to wash; only the external face is obligatory.

In wudu, Allah commands washing the face. But what exactly is the face? The Hanafi school defines it as the visible external parts. This lesson clarifies that the inner part of the lips, hidden when the mouth is closed, is not obligatory to wash. This ruling simplifies the performance of wudu and avoids unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its obligation
Wudu requires washing the face as a pillar (rukn). The exact boundary of the face is defined by custom and legal texts.
The face includes from the hairline to the chin and from ear to ear.
2
Define the boundary of the face
The face is the external part that is visible. Internal cavities (mouth, nose, eyes) are not part of the face for wudu.
This is based on the principle that only the apparent (zahir) parts are wajib.
3
Apply to the lips
When the mouth is closed, the inner lips are hidden. Following the rule that hidden parts are not wajib, the inner lips are not obligatory to wash.
The Arabic term used is 'ma inkatama qadamuhu' meaning 'that which is hidden when closed'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۸) ولا الى ما انكتم قدمه. ترجمه : (۷۸) اور منہ بند کرتے وقت اندر چھپے ہوئے ہونٹوں کا دھونا بھی واجب نہیں ہے۔
(78) Nor to the part that is hidden when the mouth is closed. Translation: (78) And washing the inner part of the lips that is hidden when the mouth is closed is also not obligatory.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement without explicit proof. It clarifies that in wudu, the inner portion of the lips that becomes hidden when the mouth is closed is not included in the obligation to wash the face. The face's obligatory wash area includes the external surfaces that are visible, but the internal mucosal area of the lips is excluded. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that the interior of the mouth is not part of the face for wudu purposes.

Key Terms
ما انكتم قدمه (ma inkatama qadamuhu): The part of the lips that is hidden (i.e., the inner surface) when the mouth is closed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for washing the inner part of the lips when the mouth is closed?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah
C) Not obligatory
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The inner lips are not wajib to wash in wudu; only the external face is obligatory.

Ruling on Washing the Beard in Wudu
Details the obligation and recommendation for washing the beard in ablution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing the beard in wudu, distinguish between thick and hanging beards, and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
For a thick beard, water flowing over suffices; for a hanging beard, khilal is recommended, not required.

In this passage, the author explains the detailed rulings regarding washing the beard during wudu. While the face includes the beard, the obligation differs depending on the density and length of the beard. The text presents several proofs from the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions to establish the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The passage begins by stating that it is not obligatory to deliver water to the hanging hair below the circle of the face. Understand the definition of the face circle (from forehead to chin).
This sets the boundary for what is fard.
2
Differentiate thick vs. hanging beard
Note the two categories: thick beard (within the face circle) and hanging beard (extending below the chin). For thick beard, the ruling is lenient; for hanging beard, an additional recommended act exists.
The distinction is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Examine proofs for thick beard
The text cites hadith where the Prophet ordered a man with a dry spot to redo wudu, and the practice of Ali pouring water from the forelock. These indicate that water flow over the surface is sufficient for the thick part.
The proofs show that the requirement is for the skin of the face, not the hair itself.
4
Examine proofs for hanging beard
The hadith of Anas and Ibn Umar show the Prophet doing takhleel. The hadith of Ibn Umar also shows he sometimes omitted it, indicating recommendation not obligation.
The command 'hākadhā amaranī rabbī' is interpreted as a recommendation due to the companion's practice.
5
Determine the hukm and evidence weight
Consolidate: For thick beard, only surface flow is fard (wajib as part of face washing). For hanging beard, takhleel is mustahabb. The proofs are ahad hadith (zanni thubut), but the ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The mufta bihi is the above. The Shafi'i position requires takhleel even for thick beard.
