وجه : (۱) رأيت عثمان بن عفان سئل عن الوضوء فدعا بماء فاتى بميضأة فاصغاها على يده اليمنى ثم ادخلها في الماء فتمضمض ثلثا واستنثر ثلثا (ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفة وضوء النی ، ص ۱۶ نمبر ۱۱۲/۱۰۸ر مسلم شریف باب صفة الوضوء و کماله، ص۱۲۳، نمبر ۵۳۸/۲۲۶) (۲) عن طلحة عن ابيه عن جده قال دخلت یعنی علی النبی الله وهو يتوضأ والماء يسيل من وجهه ولحيته وعلى صدره فرأيته يفصل بين المضمضة والاستنشاق (ابو داؤ دشریف، باب فی الفرق بين المضمضة والاستنشاق ،ص۳۰ نمبر ۱۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مضمضہ اور استنشاق الگ الگ چلو سے کیا۔ (۳) عن عاصم بن لقيط بن صبرة . .. فقلت يا رسول الله ! اخبرني عن الوضوء قال اسبغ الوضوء
Chapter on the Sunnahs of Wudu. (84) Washing the hands up to the wrists. (85) Saying the Basmalah at the beginning. (86) Using the miswak at the beginning, even with the finger when it is absent. (87) Rinsing the mouth three times, even with one handful, and snuffing water into the nose with three handfuls, and exaggeration in rinsing and snuffing for the non-fasting person, not for the fasting person. (Commentary: There are eighteen sunnahs in wudu. 1. Washing both hands up to the wrists. Explanation: Washing hands up to the wrists before beginning wudu is sunnah so that if there is impurity on the hand, it is washed off and the water does not become impure. Evidence: (1) Humran, the freed slave of Uthman, informed him that he saw Uthman bin Affan call for a vessel and poured water over his hands three times and washed them, then put his right hand into the vessel, rinsed his mouth and nose, then washed his face three times and his arms up to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet three times up to the ankles, then said: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without allowing his mind to wander, his previous sins will be forgiven. [Bukhari, Abi Dawud] In this hadith, he first washed his hands up to the wrists three times. (2) Also from Aisha, that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم performed ghusl from janabah and began by washing his palms three times. [Muslim] (85) Recite Bismillah at the beginning. Evidence: (1) Abu Sufyan bin Huwaitib from his grandmother from her father said: I heard the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم say: There is no wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah upon it. [Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud] But the meaning is that wudu is valid but no reward. (2) From al-Hasan: He said to say Bismillah when performing wudu; if he does not do it, it is sufficient. [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah] So Bismillah is sunnah. (86) Use miswak at the beginning, and if no miswak is available, use the finger. Explanation: If miswak is available, use it; if not, at least use the finger. According to the Hanafis, it is before wudu, not before prayer. Evidence: (1) From Abu Huraira: The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would have ordered them to use the miswak at every prayer. [Muslim, Tirmidhi, Bukhari] This hadith proves using miswak at prayer time, but there is an omitted phrase 'at the wudu of every prayer', i.e., miswak at the wudu of every prayer is sunnah. (2) Ibn Abbas stayed at the Prophet's house... then he returned, used the miswak, performed wudu, then stood and prayed. [Muslim] This hadith shows he used miswak before wudu, so according to Hanafis, it is before wudu. (3) From Abu Huraira: The Prophet said: Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would have ordered them to use the miswak with every wudu. [Sunan al-Bayhaqi] (4) The purpose of miswak is cleaning the mouth, so it is more appropriate with wudu. (5) Using the finger suffices for miswak, as the Prophet said: The fingers suffice for the miswak. [Sunan al-Bayhaqi] (87) Rinse the mouth three times, even with one handful; take water into the nose with three handfuls; and exaggerate in rinsing and snuffing if not fasting. Explanation: Three sunnahs are mentioned. 4th sunnah: rinse three times, whether with three separate handfuls or one handful. 5th sunnah: snuff water into nose, preferably with separate water from the mouth. 6th sunnah: exaggerate in rinsing and snuffing, provided the person is not fasting, because there is risk of water entering the stomach and breaking the fast. Evidence: (1) I saw Uthman bin Affan asked about wudu; he called for water, brought a vessel, tilted it onto his right hand, then put it in water, rinsed his mouth three times, and snuffed three times. [Abu Dawud, Muslim] (2) From Talha from his father from his grandfather: I entered upon the Prophet while he was performing wudu, water flowing from his face and beard and chest, and I saw him separating between rinsing the mouth and snuffing. [Abu Dawud] This hadith shows using separate handfuls. (3) From Asim bin Laqit bin Sabra... I said: O Messenger of Allah, tell me about wudu. He said: Perform wudu thoroughly. ...
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a classic fiqh lesson on the sunnahs of wudu, presenting six specific acts with their proofs from hadith. The author begins by stating that there are eighteen sunnahs in total but focuses on the first six here. The first sunnah is washing the hands up to the wrists before starting wudu, supported by the practice of Uthman and the Prophet in ghusl. The second sunnah is reciting Bismillah at the beginning; the author clarifies that although a hadith says 'no wudu' without it, the meaning is that the wudu is valid but without reward, making it a sunnah, not an obligation. The third sunnah is using the miswak at the beginning of wudu; the author notes a potential conflict with hadiths that mention miswak at every prayer, but the Hanafi position is that the intended meaning is 'at the wudu of every prayer', and the practice of Ibn Abbas confirms it is before wudu. If no miswak is available, using the finger suffices as per another hadith. The fourth to sixth sunnahs cover rinsing the mouth, snuffing water into the nose, and exaggeration in these acts for non-fasting persons. The author stresses that each of these acts is a sunnah, not obligatory, and provides clear hadith evidence for each, including the distinction between the mouth and nose washes being performed with separate handfuls. The lesson demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving sunnahs from the Prophet's actions and statements, and clarifies the precise conditions, such as the prohibition of exaggeration for the fasting person to avoid breaking the fast.

Key Terms
سنن الوضوء (sunan al-wudu): The recommended acts (sunnah) during the performance of wudu, which are not obligatory but carry reward.
مبالغة (mubalaghah): Exaggeration in rinsing the mouth and snuffing water up the nose, meaning to do so thoroughly, but not for the fasting person.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Snuffing water into the nose during wudu, typically done three times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on saying Bismillah at the beginning of wudu?
A) It is fard, and wudu is invalid without it.
B) It is wajib, and leaving it requires sajdah sahw.
C) It is sunnah; wudu is valid without it but reward is less.
D) It is sunnah only if one remembers; otherwise not.

Key Takeaway
The six sunnahs of wudu are confirmed recommendations; omitting them does not invalidate wudu but misses reward.

The Sunnah of Siwak at the Time of Wudu
Establishes siwak as sunnah at wudu through multiple hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal status of siwak at wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain the primary hadith proof that establishes it as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Siwak at wudu is sunnah mu'akkadah — recommended but not obligatory, proven by the Prophet's conditional statement.

The use of siwak (toothstick) is a highly emphasized sunnah in the Hanafi school, particularly at the time of wudu. This lesson examines the hadith proofs that establish its recommendation and distinguishes it from an obligation. By understanding the Prophet's phrasing, you will see why the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah mu'akkadah rather than wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is using siwak at the time of wudu. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah, a highly recommended practice.
Not wajib, not fard.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The key hadith from Sahih Muslim and Sunan al-Bayhaqi: 'If it were not that I would burden my nation, I would have commanded them to use siwak with every wudu.'
The conditional 'if not that I would burden' is crucial.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The conditional phrase indicates that the command is not absolute; thus the act is recommended, not obligatory. The phrase 'with every wudu' explicitly links siwak to wudu.
This is the Hanafi usul: a conditional command indicates sunnah, not wajib.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school emphasizes siwak at prayer times. The Hanafi school reconciles by understanding that wudu is the occasion for prayer, so the sunnah attaches to wudu.
This difference is about timing, not obligation.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
Siwak is sunnah mu'akkadah at wudu, preferably before beginning wudu. Using it brings reward; omitting it does not affect the validity of wudu.
The fifth hadith shows that if siwak is unavailable, fingers suffice, indicating its non-obligatory nature.

Source Text

وجه : (ا) عن ابي هريرة رضي الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لولا ان اشق على المؤمنين و في حديث زهير على امتى لامرتهم بالسواك عند كل صلوة (مسلم شريف) (۲) ان ابن عباس حدثه انه بات عند نبي الله .... ثم رجع فتسوک فتوضأ ثم قام فصلی (مسلم شريف) (۳) عن ابي هريرة رضى الله عنه قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لولا ان اشـق عـلـى امتى لامرتهم بالسواك مع كل وضوء (سنن بيھقي) (۵) عن انس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : تجزى من السواك الاصابع (سنن بيھقي)
Proof: (1) From Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, he said: 'If it were not that I would burden the believers' – and in the hadith of Zuhayr: 'my nation' – 'I would have commanded them to use the siwak at every prayer.' (Muslim). (2) That Ibn Abbas narrated to him that he spent the night with the Prophet of Allah... then he returned, used siwak, performed wudu, then stood and prayed. (Muslim). (3) From Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'If it were not that I would burden my nation, I would have commanded them to use siwak with every wudu.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). (5) From Anas, from the Prophet, peace be upon him, he said: 'Fingers suffice for the siwak.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section that establishes the sunnah of using siwak (toothstick) at the time of wudu. The author provides several hadith proofs. The first hadith mentions siwak at every prayer, which is interpreted by Hanafi scholars as meaning at the wudu for each prayer, due to the word 'wudu' in the third hadith. The second hadith shows the Prophet's practice of using siwak before wudu. The third hadith explicitly links siwak to wudu. The fourth (omitted) is a rational proof. The fifth hadith allows using fingers if siwak is unavailable, indicating its sunnah status is not strict. These proofs together establish that siwak is sunnah mu'akkadah at wudu, not wajib, as the hadith says 'if not that I would burden' indicating its recommendation.

Key Terms
سواك (siwak): A stick used for cleaning teeth, derived from the arak tree, used as a sunnah act.

Key Takeaway
Siwak at wudu is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, based on the Prophet's conditional command; using it brings reward, and omitting it does not invalidate wudu.

The Sunnah of Madmadah, Istinshaq, and Mubalaghah in Wudu
Ruling and proofs for madmadah, istinshaq, and mubalaghah in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for madmadah, istinshaq, and mubalaghah, identify their proofs, and distinguish them from fard acts.

Core Idea
Madmadah, istinshaq, and mubalaghah are sunnah mu'akkadah in Hanafi fiqh, not fard or wajib.

This lesson covers three recommended acts (sunan) during wudu: rinsing the mouth (madmadah), sniffing water into the nose (istinshaq), and exaggerating in both (mubalaghah). The Hanafi school holds these as highly emphasized sunnah, based on the Prophet's practice and explicit command for non-fasting persons. Understanding their graded status helps ensure correct wudu performance without confusion with obligatory acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their ruling
Read the source text to determine the hukm for madmadah, istinshaq, and mubalaghah. Note that they are sunnah mu'akkadah.
Sunnah mu'akkadah means a confirmed recommended act; omitting it does not invalidate wudu.
2
Examine the first proof: practice of Uthman
The narration of Uthman performing madmadah and istinshaq three times each demonstrates the prophetic sunnah.
This shows the number of times and the method.
3
Examine the second proof: separation between madmadah and istinshaq
The hadith of Talhah shows the Prophet separating the two acts, indicating they are distinct sunan.
This refutes the view that they must be combined.
4
Examine the third proof: command and exception for fasting
The explicit command 'asbigh' for istinshaq, qualified for non-fasting, shows it is sunnah not wajib, and mubalaghah is prohibited for fasting.
The exception ('lighayr al-sa'im') indicates the ruling is specific.
5
Understand the Hanafi position on ikhtilaf
Some schools consider these acts wajib; the Hanafi school differs based on the zanni nature of the evidence.
Note the difference in thubut and dalala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمضمضة ثلاثا ولو بغرفة و الاستنشاق بثلاث غرفات و المبالغة في المضمضة والاستنشاق لغير الصائم. وجه : (۱) رأيت عثمان بن عفان سئل عن الوضوء فدعا بماء فاتى بميضأة فاصغاها على يده اليمنى ثم ادخلها في الماء فتمضمض ثلثا واستنثر ثلثا. (۲) عن طلحة عن ابيه عن جده قال دخلت یعنی علی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو يتوضأ والماء يسيل من وجهه ولحيته وعلى صدره فرأيته يفصل بين المضمضة والاستنشاق. And rinsing the mouth three times, even with one handful, and taking water into the nose with three handfuls, and exaggeration in rinsing the mouth and nose for one who is not fasting. Proof: (1) I saw Uthman ibn Affan was asked about wudu: he called for water, a vessel was brought, he tilted it onto his right hand, then inserted it into the water, rinsed his mouth three times, and cleaned his nose three times. (2) From Talhah, from his father, from his grandfather, he said: I entered upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, while he was performing wudu, water flowing from his face and beard and chest, and I saw him separate between rinsing the mouth and nose. (3) From Asim ibn Laqit ibn Sabrah... I said: O Messenger of Allah, tell me about wudu. He said: Perform wudu thoroughly and sniff water into the nose, except if you are fasting.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section on three sunan of wudu: madmadah (rinsing mouth), istinshaq (sniffing water into nose), and mubalaghah (exaggeration) in both. The ruling states that madmadah is sunnah three times, even if using one handful of water, and istinshaq with three separate handfuls. Mubalaghah is sunnah for non-fasting persons to avoid water reaching the throat. The proofs include: (1) The practice of Uthman showing three times for each. (2) The Prophet separating between madmadah and istinshaq, indicating distinct acts. (3) The explicit command to perform istinshaq thoroughly for non-fasting persons, implying prohibition for fasting. These are sunnah, not wajib, as the acts are demonstrated by the Prophet but not commanded in Quran.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water, moving it around and then spitting out.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Taking water into the nose and then expelling it.
مبالغة (mubalaghah): Exaggeration in reaching water deep into the mouth/nose without harm.

Key Takeaway
Madmadah, istinshaq, and mubalaghah are sunnah mu'akkadah in Hanafi fiqh; they are not fard or wajib, and mubalaghah is not for fasting.

The Sunnah of Takhleel al-Lihyah (Beard) in Wudu
Ruling and proof for running fingers through thick beard during wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on takhleel al-lihyah, explain the proof from hadith, and distinguish between the Hanafi and other school positions.

Core Idea
Takhleel of a thick beard is sunnah, not wajib, because the Prophet's command was specific to him.

When performing wudu, a person with a thick beard should run wet fingers through it from underneath. This act, called takhleel al-lihyah, is based on explicit Prophetic practice. But is it obligatory or recommended? The Hanafi school answers with precision, analyzing the Prophet's own words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, understand what takhleel al-lihyah is: running wet fingers through the beard from underneath. The Hanafi ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) for a thick beard, not wajib.
The term 'kaththah' (thick) is a condition—this sunnah is only for a beard that is thick enough that water may not reach the skin easily.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites two hadith: (1) Anas reports the Prophet performed takhleel and said 'Thus my Lord commanded me.' (2) Ibn Umar describes the method: rubbing cheeks first, then interlocking the beard with fingers from below.
Both are ahad hadith (single-chained narrations), with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase 'hāka dhā amaranī rabbī' (thus my Lord commanded me) is central. In Hanafi usul, the word 'amaranī' (commanded me) indicates specificity to the Prophet (khulusiyyah), not a general obligation for the Ummah.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position: if the command were general, it would be wajib; but the specificity reduces it to sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., some Shafi'i views) consider takhleel wajib for a thick beard, citing the same hadith but interpreting 'amaranī' as a general command through the Prophet to the Ummah.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): if omitted, wudu is still valid in Hanafi (since sunnah), but in other views it might be deficient.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the context and additional narrations that indicate the Prophet did not command the whole Ummah explicitly. Thus, takhleel remains a sunnah, not an obligation.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is sunnah muakkadah; one should do it to follow the Sunnah but omitting it does not invalidate wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تخليل اللحية الكثة بكف ماء من اسفلها. وجه : (۱) عن انس بن مالك ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان اذا توضأ أخذ كفا من ماء فأدخله تحت حنكه فخلل به لحيته، و قال هكذا امرني ربي عز و جل. (۲) عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا توضأ عرك عارضيه بعض العرك ثم شبك لحيته بأصابعه من تحتها.
Running fingers through a thick beard with a handful of water from underneath. Proof: (1) From Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he performed wudu, took a handful of water, inserted it under his chin, and ran it through his beard, and said: 'Thus my Lord, the Mighty and Majestic, commanded me.' (2) From Ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when he performed wudu, rubbed his cheeks a little, then interlocked his beard with his fingers from underneath.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof section on the sunnah of takhleel al-lihyah (running fingers through the beard) during wudu. The ruling specifies that this is done for a thick beard (kaththah), with a handful of water from underneath the chin. The proof includes two hadith: (1) Anas reports the Prophet doing it, with the explicit statement that Allah commanded him to do so, indicating its importance but not obligation. (2) Ibn Umar's narration shows the method of rubbing the cheeks first then interlocking the beard from below. Hanafis hold that takhleel is sunnah, not wajib, because the command in the first hadith is specifically to the Prophet (khulusiyyah) and not a general obligation. For a sparse beard, it is not emphasized.

Key Terms
تخليل اللحية (takhleel al-lihyah): Running wet fingers through the beard to ensure water reaches the roots.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that takhleel al-lihyah is sunnah muakkadah for a thick beard, based on the Prophet's practice and his statement indicating specificity.

Washing Each Limb Three Times in Wudu: A Confirmed Sunnah
Ruling and proof for washing each wudu limb three times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing wudu limbs three times and identify the proof from the hadith of Uthman.

Core Idea
Washing each limb three times in wudu is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation.

In wudu, the basic fard is to wash each limb once. However, the Prophet's practice was to wash each limb three times, and he encouraged his followers to do the same. This lesson examines the ruling and the evidence from a well-known hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing each wudu limb three times. According to the Hanafi school, this is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah). The fard requirement is a single wash.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a recommended practice that the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated by Humran, the freed slave of Uthman, who witnessed Uthman performing wudu by washing each limb three times. Uthman then attributed this practice to the Prophet.
This hadith is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and other collections.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement 'whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine' indicates that the three-time washing is part of his sunnah. The specific demonstration by Uthman, who was a companion, shows the Prophetic practice.
The term 'nāḥū wuḍū'ī hādhā' (like this wudu of mine) makes the three washes a prescribed sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no major ikhtilaf among the schools regarding the recommendation of three washes. All agree it is mustahabb. Some early scholars debated whether a second or third wash is bid'ah, but the consensus is that it is sunnah.
The Hanafi position is clear: one wash fulfills the fard; three is the complete sunnah.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is that washing three times is sunnah mu'akkadah. One should strive to do it, but if done less, the wudu is still valid.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is widely relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غسل كل عضو ثلاثاً. وجه : ان حمران مولی عثمان اخبره انه رأى عثمان بن عفان دعا باناء، فافرغ على كفيه ثلاث مرار فغسلهما، ثم ادخل يمينه فى الاناء فمضمض و استنثر ثم غسل وجهه ثلاثا و يديه الى المرفقين ثلاث مرار، ثم مسح برأسه، ثم غسل رجليه ثلاث مرار الى الكعبين، ثم قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: من توضأ نحو وضوئى هذا ثم صلى ركعتين لايحدث فيهما نفسه غفر له ما تقدم من ذنبه.
Washing each limb three times. Proof: That Humran, the freed slave of Uthman, informed him that he saw Uthman ibn Affan call for a vessel, then he poured water over his hands three times and washed them, then he inserted his right hand into the vessel and rinsed his mouth and cleaned his nose, then washed his face three times, and his arms up to the elbows three times, then wiped his head, then washed his feet up to the ankles three times, then said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine, then prays two rak'ahs without speaking to himself (about worldly matters), will have his previous sins forgiven.'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof section establishing that washing each limb three times in wudu is sunnah. The proof is a famous hadith from Humran reporting the complete wudu of Uthman, which he attributes to the Prophet. The Prophet explicitly says 'whoever performs wudu like this wudu of mine' indicating that the three-time washing is part of the sunnah practice. The hadith also shows the order: hands, mouth/nose, face, arms, wiping head, feet. Hanafis hold that washing three times is sunnah, not fard; once is sufficient for the fard, and three is the recommended complete form. The additional promise of forgiveness for two rak'ahs after such wudu emphasizes its virtue.

Key Terms
غسل ثلاثاً (ghusl thalathan): Washing each limb three times in wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, must wash three times
C) Yes, perfectly valid with no deficiency
D) No, it is invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that washing each wudu limb three times is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation; one wash suffices for validity.

The Ruling of Khilal of the Thick Beard
Explaining the sunnah of passing water through thick beard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khilal of the thick beard in wudu and distinguish it from wajib based on the Prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
Khilal of the thick beard is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.

This lesson explains the Hanafi position on khilal (passing water through) the thick beard during wudu. While some schools consider it obligatory, the Hanafi school holds it to be a strongly recommended sunnah. We will examine the textual evidence and the reasoning behind this classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what khilal is and the hukm level assigned by the Hanafi school.
The text explicitly states it is sunnah, the seventh sunnah of wudu.
2
Understand the distinction from wajib
Recognize that reaching water inside the thick beard is not obligatory; the obligation is to wash the face, and the beard is part of the face.
Khilal is an additional recommended act.
3
Examine the Prophetic evidence
Analyse the two hadith cited: the Prophet's action and his statement 'Thus my Lord commanded me'.
The command is interpreted as a recommendation, not an obligation, based on Hanafi usul.
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Recognize that the Shafi'i school considers khilal wajib, but the Hanafi school's position is sunnah.
The difference stems from how each school interprets the imperative in the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۸۸) ایک چلو پانی سے گھنی ڈاڑھی کے نیچے کی جانب سے خلال کرنا۔
تشریح :[1] یہ ساتویں سنت ہے۔ گھنی ڈاڑھی کے اندر پانی پہنچا نا واجب نہیں ہے البتہ خلال کرنا سنت ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان اذا توضأ أخذ كفا من ماء فأدخله تحت حنكه فخلل به لحیته ، و قال هكذا امرني ربي عز و جل ۔ (ابوداود شریف، باب تخلیل اللحیة، ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۱۴۵ ترمذی شریف، باب تخلیل اللحیة، ص ۱۴، نمبر ۳۱ را ابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء فی تخلیل اللحية ، ص ۶۳ نمبر ۴۲۹) (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ لٹکی ہوئی ڈاڑھی میں خلال فرمایا کرتے تھے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا توضأ عرك عارضيه بعض العرك ثم شبك لحيته بأصابعه من تحتها - ابن ماجه شریف، باب ما جاءت خلیل اللحية، ص ۶۳ نمبر ۴۳۲ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نیچے سے خلال کرے۔
Translation: (88) Khilal of the thick beard with a handful of water from underneath. Explanation: This is the seventh sunnah. Reaching water inside the thick beard is not obligatory, but khilal is sunnah. Evidence: (1) In this hadith: from Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when performing wudu, took a handful of water and inserted it under his chin and then passed it through his beard, and said: 'Thus my Lord commanded me.' (2) In this hadith: that he used to perform khilal of the hanging beard. From Ibn Umar: the Prophet (peace be upon him) when performing wudu, rubbed his cheeks somewhat and then intertwined his beard with his fingers from underneath. In this hadith he performed khilal from underneath.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage explains the sunnah of khilal of the thick beard. The author states it is the seventh sunnah of wudu. He clarifies that it is not wajib to ensure water reaches the skin under a thick beard; rather, the sunnah is to pass water through it. Two hadith proofs are given: one from Anas ibn Malik where the Prophet takes a handful of water and passes it through his beard, and another from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice of passing fingers through the beard from underneath. The Hanafi position is that this act is sunnah, not fard or wajib. The text emphasizes performing khilal from underneath the beard.

Key Terms
تخليل (takhlil): Passing water or fingers through the beard to ensure water reaches the hair and skin beneath.
اللحية الكثة (al-lihyah al-kaththa): A thick, dense beard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of performing khilal of the thick beard in wudu according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Khilal of the thick beard is a sunnah muakkadah act in wudu, not an obligation.
